From: Joseph Koshy <joseph.koshy@gmail.com >
Date: Oct 31, 2007 10:15 AM
Subject: Nice summary of FreeBSD 7.X

Howdy all,

Here is a nice summary of the performance characteristics (and new features)
of the upcoming FreeBSD 7 release:

   http://people.freebsd.org/~kris/scaling/7.0%20Preview.pdf<http://people.freebsd.org/%7Ekris/scaling/7.0%20Preview.pdf>

Per the graphs in the paper,  on the MySQL benchmark, Linux 2.6.22 is 15%
slower than FreeBSD  7 (using the ULE scheduler).   Linux v2.6.23 with the
much
publicized  "completely fair" scheduler turns out to be much slower than
v2.6.22, at approx 75% of the performance of FreeBSD 7+ULE.

Regards,
Koshy

Hi  Ramadas,
Any domain registrar will allow name server changing option(and other domain
control options), else they cant host their site at all :)
In domains.webspace2host.com also all the standard options are there.

But what Sam Sharma asks is Managed DNS option i.e. option to add A record,
CNAME record etc... and domain forwarding options.

These are additional services which are usually charged extra by any domain
registrars.
These options will generally be available free thro CPanel/WHM by the web
space providers.

Regards,
Mugunth

On Thu, 1 Nov 2007 16:15:14 +0530 (IST), Mahalingam Subramaniam
<smal@ccmb.res.in> said:  

> Hi Luggies how to assign root privilege to non-root user so that
> he/she becomes sys admin during regular root user absence? 

        If this is a one time thing, why not change root password, give
 the new password to the temporary root, and change it back when the
 regular admin returns?

        If it is an ongoing thing, sudo can achieve similar things -- the
 difference is that you give and take away sudo rights as needed. Or
 consider trusting the junior admin (I mean, if they mean to do harm,
 they can do so when the cat is away).

        manoj

> when the product is good, packaging is irrelevant. We are not selling

> other is in the packaging. We are doing FOSS, so why not call it a
> FOSS Conference? The name is not important - what we do is important.

 welcome to real world. Give some one the best of teh products without
branding/packaging for free, chances are they will throw it in
dustbin. Gift wrap a bad product and charge a premium people love it.
Todays world is driven by packaging and this is a mistake every FOSS
conference makes.
 If only good products were to succeed  winblows would have failed to
see the day of light. Good packaging is equally important.

Subject: [Ilugc] debian dist-upgrade change encoding?
Message-ID: <51702CA7-38C6-407A-B7F9-C543E489ECE0@thenilgiris.com>

hi,

I had a bunch of postgres databases on my server which were (as far  
as I know) set to unicode. They were happily accepting tamil, telugu,  
finnish etc characters. Recently I got complaints that the databases  
were barfing on non-ascii characters - so they were. I looked and  
found to my horror that most of them were in Latin1 encoding. Is it  
possible that a dist-upgrade could change the encoding of the  
databases from unicode to Latin1? An example is http:// 
nrcfosshelpline.in/code/. This database was all along accepting tamil  
characters. After the dist-upgrade it is no longer doing so.

From rajanvn at gmail.com  Fri Nov  2 21:59:35 2007
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Fri Nov  2 21:59:54 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Help needed
In-Reply-To: <ed2d3c000711020133t7d711aa5qaea030e277709eb6@mail.gmail.com>
References: <ed2d3c000711020133t7d711aa5qaea030e277709eb6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e977d4310711020929r441234bag79973e3dafc4a06a@mail.gmail.com>

On Nov 2, 2007 2:03 PM, ?????????? <citizenofgnu@gmail.com> wrote:
> I have an xml file and my requirement is to build a mysql table and
> push the value of the xml file into the table.
> I would request a pointer on how to build a table at run time after
> look the xsd file. Is there any straight way tool for solving the
> problem, I heard xmlspy solves the problem.

XML Spy costs a fortune.

How often do you get new Schemas and how often do you want to create
these tables? Once during design time or is it in run time? How big is
your schema going to be? Looks like you are doing some B2B stuff?

If you are in the Java world, I would create convert the XSD into a
set of Value Objects (POJO alias beans alias Records/Struct in the
C/C++ world). I would then manually create the tables that map on to
the beans. Java Hibernate does have an option to create the tables
from these beans. But still we do have to code a little. I haven't
tried the last part yet, myself.

I don't prefer to use an automated tool to create a DB Schema using an
XML Schema.  I consider that risky. Consider the different name spaces
and some in-efficient  XSDs that can be given as inputs.  You might
end up creating redundant tables due to a bad XSD. The Table naming
conventions would take you for a ride if you do it
automatically.Sorry, if I sounded a little discouraging.

OOPS... I remembered just now. You work on PHP right? Sorry, I don't
have a direct answer for your question. But the answer that I gave
might help others (may be?). But if you want to understand how to get
a pointer on how to do some "intelligent and manual" mapping between
XSD and DB Schema, I can send you a detailed mail on that?

Regards,
Natarajan
From rajanvn at gmail.com  Fri Nov  2 22:13:20 2007
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Fri Nov  2 22:13:34 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] implement java file in c++
In-Reply-To: <20071102102202.839a85ae@mail.redim.net>
References: <20071102102202.839a85ae@mail.redim.net>
Message-ID: <e977d4310711020943u6fac7e45i7e92268af51fc819@mail.gmail.com>

On Nov 2, 2007 3:52 PM, Yogesh Kumar K <yogeshk@redim.net> wrote:
> i am using the code of a Game in C++ .

What kind of game? High graphics/ 3D games or strategy/text based games?

>now i need to add java Game  also .
> how to add a java files from C++ code .is it possible java files to be  used .
> any possible to import Java files or include java files in c++ is possible .

Is it possible to call a C++ code from Java?
Yes it is possible using JNI API (you have to do some coding here).
With this you can call functions and APIs written in C++ into Java.

Is it possible to call a Java Class from C++ ?
Yes, you can using a system call to invoke the JVM and then passing
the MAIN class name as a parameter

Is it possible to call a particular java class's method alone from C++?
I don't think so.

Did I answer your question?


Regards,
Natarajan

Sir,
     In my Acer PC (AMD athlon), System date is frequently changed abruptly.
To synchronize the  RTC(hardware) with system date and time( software), I
edit grub as

kernel /vmlinuz-2.6.9-22.EL ro root=LABEL=/ rhgb quiet *noapic acpi=off*
Now system will not switched off automatically during shutdown.

Any other Idea to set an RTC date and Time with system date and time?

N.Padmanthan.

From solar345 at gmail.com  Sat Nov  3 23:16:34 2007
From: solar345 at gmail.com (Antano Solar)
Date: Sat Nov  3 23:16:50 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Help needed
In-Reply-To: <ed2d3c000711020133t7d711aa5qaea030e277709eb6@mail.gmail.com>
References: <ed2d3c000711020133t7d711aa5qaea030e277709eb6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <b2600ec40711031046o5fe514e9tf23b548890d03e3e@mail.gmail.com>

On Nov 2, 2007 2:03 PM, ?????????? <citizenofgnu@gmail.com> wrote:

> Dear Friends,
>
>
> I have an xml file and my requirement is to build a mysql table and
> push the value of the xml file into the table.
> I would request a pointer on how to build a table at run time after
> look the xsd file. Is there any straight way tool for solving the
> problem, I heard xmlspy solves the problem. Any pointer is much
> appreciated.
>
>
1. There is a berkley xml embedded database  (opensource) by oracle . Needs
no setup , has binding in most language. DB is stores in flat file similar
to sqlite.Very efficient and fast.Supports xpath and xquery.

2.You can try the traditional method of having something map the xml to
conventional DB. as usual you have 101 ways to do this in perl . One of
which would be . DBIx::DBStag  ->
http://search.cpan.org/~cmungall/DBIx-DBStag-0.09/DBIx/DBStag.pm<http://search.cpan.org/%7Ecmungall/DBIx-DBStag-0.09/DBIx/DBStag.pm>
.
By the DBIx in the above module is a database abstraction layer which
supports any database type.So you can theoritically take the xml file and
store it as tables in conventional DB or to ldap or to xml file system or
even to facebook.
Besides that , even a perl paranoid programmer can use it , as like almost
all perl modules on cpan , there is working code in the synopsis section of
the documentation . You will have to just take the code change 1 line - the
db connection string. Then you can use it as a stand alone program which you
can invoke from other programs.



Antano Solar John

to keep your version of the configuration file or if you want to use the
package maintainer's version.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Nov  5 16:52:15 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Nov  5 16:41:24 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] CFP - FOSS Conference '08
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0711051452270.1059-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

CALL FOR PARTICIPATION

The Indian Linux Users Group, Chennai[1] Chapter, in association with
NRC-FOSS[2], Chennai take great pleasure in inviting you to
participate in the FOSS Conference to be held at MIT, Chromepet,
Chennai from noon on Friday Feb 1st 2008 to noon on Sunday Feb 3rd
2008.

THE ORGANISERS

ILUGC is one of the oldest lugs in the country and has been
continuously active since it was founded. It keeps a low profile and
specialises in grass roots work all around Tamilnadu (and in the
neighbouring states too). Under it's guidance, many lugs are active in
colleges and towns all around Tamilnadu. At the same time, ILUGC
members are in the forefront of the FOSS movement both at the national
and international level.

NRC-FOSS, a Central Government Project, funded by the DIT and jointly
run by CDAC and AU-KBC, Chennai, for the past two and half years has
been actively promoting FOSS in the academic domain. It's main focus
has been getting FOSS introduced into the curriculum of Engineering
Colleges in the country. Also apart from encouraging student projects
in FOSS, it has been active in encouraging academia to release it's
work under FOSS/Creative Commons licenses. AU-KBC Research Centre,
MIT, Chennai has strengths in NLP, Bio-informatics, Wireless,
Cryptography and Embedded computing, much of which uses FOSS tools 
and has released some of this research as FOSS.

SCOPE

The conference will focus on new users/contributors to FOSS.

As Audience: First timers or newcomers.

As Speakers: First time speakers.

As contributors: Students who are doing their projects, academic
personal who have worked with FOSS tools but are yet to release their
work, and, of course, the huge surge of new users in the government
domain. At the same time, provide a forum for interaction for more
experienced developers who will be coming to the conference.

CALL FOR PARTICIPATION

We invite participation in the following areas - in order of importance.

1. Delegates to the conference. There is no fun in having a conference
if there is no audience. Our primary focus is on audience. Please
register as a delegate and encourage your friends to do so. We cannot
guarantee transport and accommodation, but if you have a group of
people who want to come and let us know early enough, we will try to
get your travel and accommodation sponsored.

2. Volunteers. Volunteers are the lifeblood of a conference and will
be treated as privileged persons. Volunteers are needed at the
conference venue for myriad tasks. But, more important, are volunteers
from outside Chennai who are needed to contact students, teachers,
government employees and get them to come for the conference. We
envisage holding training camps for teachers and government employees
- and will do so if we are able to convince enough of them to come. We
can send people to address meetings to motivate people to come - if
you organise the meetings.

3. Sprints. A FOSS conference that does not contribute documentation/
code is worthless. A sprint is where a group of people sit together
and finish a task. We have had sprints before, once in Loyola college
to do translation, and again, last year at MIT to do translation. A
sprint can be for translating applications, mass fixing of bugs, doing
long pending documentation, writing code etc,. Sprints need to be
carefully planned, tasks laid down before hand, participants fixed,
facilities arranged. If you are interested in organising a sprint,
please register and attend the meeting in January for finalising
proposed sprints. Since this is an entry-level conference, please be
aware that you may need a day to train volunteers for the sprint
before actually starting it. Some ideas: making a comprehensive list to
be uploaded to the ILUGD Hall of Shame websites, completing a list of
all lugs in India, making a directory of FOSS contributors in India,
contribute to the OpenMoko project ...

4. Student projects in FOSS. We will give special place to student
projects in FOSS - past, present and future. Now is the time for your
project - register and exhibit it at the conference. Prizes will be
given for the best projects.

5. Formal academic projects using FOSS tools. There are a huge number
of these lying unsung in university and government archives. We invite
academics to present their work here.

6. Talks. On any aspect of FOSS except installation issues. Talks will
be of 30 minutes duration with 15 minutes for discussion. note:  
installation demos will be arranged anyway

7. Mini talks - one hall will be reserved for this. 10 minute talk
followed by 5 questions.

8. Cultural contests - drawings, paintings, skits, dances ... with
FOSS as the theme. Prizes will be given for the best performances

9. Sub-conferences and BOFs - these will largely be left to be
organised by those who propose them. Facilities will be provided as
needed.

10. Workshops for teachers and government employees will be organised
by the conference organisers depending on demand.

11. The registration website will be up in a day or two. Kindly
forward this CFP to all LUG, GLUG and FSUG mailing lists.

[1] ILUGC   : http://www.chennailug.org/
[2] NRC-FOSS: http://nrcfosshelpline.in/

Thanks,
-- 
Bharathi S

purpose of the event is to allow users to explore the benefits of MySQL 
Enterprise are now available. The roadshow will feature exclusive 
seminars, and networking events along with an opportunity to brush 
shoulders with the MySQL co-founder and vice president David Axmark and 
senior vice president of MySQL Asia Pacific Larry Stefonic, and other 
MySQL representatives right here in India.

The roadshow will start on 6 November and will run till 8 November 2007.
The cities which will witness the roadrash are:

Bangalore: 6th November 2007
Delhi:  7th November 2007
Chennai:  8th November 2007

The admission to the event is free if you are pre-registered.

To register now, contact kmihashi@mysql.com

From writetojanani at gmail.com  Tue Nov  6 11:09:33 2007
From: writetojanani at gmail.com (Janani Gopalakrishnan)
Date: Tue Nov  6 11:11:21 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: FOSS Conference @ Chennai
References: <3e4fd9970711012223s1bb083di684f52ce660bd2b9@mail.gmail.com><20071105142854.GA6401@frodo.hserus.net.hserus.net><3e4fd9970711050803g44f67230w92aa1a60cfe1cf24@mail.gmail.com>
	<200711061055.04994.shriramadhas@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <00ec01c82037$6aa97640$6401a8c0@JANANI>

>> And what make you think that a tamil name will prevent from people
>> around the country to participate ?

It won't actually prevent them from participating, but the naming process 
becomes complicated, because you not only have to come up with a name but an 
explanation for it as well, since it will not be self-explanatory to those 
who don't understand Tamil.

Plus, there is a basic rule for branding -- the name should be simple, 
easy-to-pronounce and have a high recall potential. If an Indic language 
name is adopted, it might not be easy for others to pronounce or remember. 
My name is just three syllables - ja+na+ni, but I have heard it pronounced 
in the worst possible ways by people unfamiliar with it! A similar fate 
might befall the event's name if chosen from Indic vocabulary.

Also, how then will the event be publicised by word-of-mouth? It will 
become, 'the name that begins with <some alphabet>', or 'the event organised 
by Chennai-LUG and NRCFOSS', or 'the event for new-comers to FOSS' etc, and 
the actual name of the event will hardly get propagated. That is not good in 
the long-run.

Ironical though it is, today, choosing an Indic name seems more chauvinistic 
than choosing an English name -- because more people seem to be able to 
read/write/pronounce English better than the language of their neighbouring 
State!

Cheers,
Jan

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Nov  6 11:52:41 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Nov  6 11:52:48 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: FOSS Conference @ Chennai
Message-ID: <36496.61.247.255.58.1194330161.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

On Monday 05 November 2007 21:33:57 vivek khurana wrote:
> ??And what make you think that a tamil name will prevent from people
> around the country to participate ?

Unless your exhibition is very well known, it is best to stick to commonly
understood names in a common language (English). Some one from the north
or other parts of south india won't be able to figure out what the
exhibition is about if the name doesn't make any sense to them.

For instance, the FLOSS conference held annually in France has the name:
"Rencontres Mondiales du Logiciel Libre" or RMIL for short. How many
non-french speaking users will even think that this is a IT related
conference let alone a FLOSS conference?

Technical terms are quite difficult to understand when written in a
different language than what they are normally communicated in.

No one becomes a better person because of knowing one language or the
other .. or by promoting one language or the other. So lets leave all this
linguistic chauvinism at the door instead of flooding this list with all
the linguistic flag waving.

Regards,
PK

On 06-Nov-07, at 12:40 PM, Dee?an Chakravarthy wrote:

> 1)Do you use any open source conference management system ?  If  
> needed I can volunteer to install CGPublisher and maintain it for  
> the conference.
> Please take a look at  http://www.cgpublisher.com/
> 2)If you want to use other publishing system, then I'm ok with.

as you may have noticed, the format of this conference is a bit  
unusual. It is not following the standard 'call for papers' -  
'deadline' - 'review' - 'suspence: is my paper chosen?' -  
'acceptance' method. Also, we are giving priority to audience,  
outstation volunteers, student projects, sprints which most standard  
software doesnt handle - so we will be rolling our own software for  
that. We probably will not have a deadline, and hope the papers,  
sprints, projects etc, will be self-selecting.

> 3)Is the conference multi threaded ?  If so what are the different  
> streams ?

no formal streams - lets see what is submitted first, then we may  
make it into streams

My Few Cents..

[1] Name : FOSS Conference 2008 @ Chennai.

Simple as of now and we can change the year and place next year
provided we are going to move over to Tier 2 cities.

[2] As Vamsee said, Localization can be a track or sub-conference
under this main-conference and we can have a localized name for it.
This will also enable other enthusiastic groups to have their own sub
conferences, such as ChennaiPy group.

[3] As Raman said this is the first time that we are organizing such a
big event. Though we have very good experience in organizing things
like LDD and workshops, conferences are really different. Hence we may
miss some points and we may over look certain things. Bringing it to
our focus will help us in correcting them :)

We expect all our members to offer a supporting hand and help us make
this a success, but still constructive criticisms are welcomed please
forbid from growing the thread and digressing too much.

@Bharathi,

Please close this "name hunt" soon so we can proceed discussing other
things. Else this is getting into a tail with no end. :)

On Tuesday 06 November 2007 21:40:15 Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
>  Prema getting pronounced as Brema ..

[OT]

i analysed this quite a bit and there are two possible reasons that came to me 
from sources i approached..

1) the four "ka" etc., sounding should have existed in tamil and letter 
representation for them should have gone in the medival ages.

2) non native tamil words have such problems and such words should have been 
derived from sanskrit etc.,  

there are rules in tamil grammer as to where it should be "ka" etc., and where 
it should be "ga" 

practise makes it perfect or knowledge of grammar helps...

like a "ka" as in "kalvi" is pronouced as 'ka' and 'ka' as in 'vaanka' is 
pronounced as 'ga'

when some one mis-spells as in case of "Brema", its root as it is clear in 
this case is sanskrit

remember this is not the case 
in 'pavalam', 'paarthiban', 'pani, 'pallavan', 'paar', 'parisu', 'pattiyal', 'pendatti', 'pillai', 'pasumai' 'pari' 'pazhi' 
etc.,

while its 'ba' is the following,

'panbu' 'anbu' 'thembu' 'kambu' 'thambi' 

when its its own 'mei' that comes before its again lighter

'thappi', 'seruppu', 'appavi' etc.,

there are set of rules defined..

3) grantha letters are even now in use sa, sha,  ja for this purpose and the 
script of grantha is south-indian.

and it goes on...

--

Subject: [Ilugc] Google's Open Source Mobile Platform
Message-ID: <1ab22a4b0711061213p639134b1wfdb3c607114d62d1@mail.gmail.com>

Hi all,
          Google's Open Source Mobile Platform :
As expected, today  Google took the wraps off of the gPhone (as the
media have for months been referring to the rumored project). Google
is "leading a broad industry alliance to transform mobile phones into
powerful mobile computers," and will be licensing its software to all
comers on an open source basis under the Apache license. (The Wall
Street Journal's Ben Worthen demonstrates a miserable grasp of what
"open source" means.) Google's US partners include Nextel and Sprint,
but not AT&T nor Verizon. Phones will be available in the second half
of 2008 ? not the spring as earlier reports had speculated. News.com's
analysis warns that Google won't take over the mobile market
overnight, though they quote Forrester in the opinion that Google may
be one of the three biggest mobile players after several years of
shakeout.

>From : http://linux.slashdot.org/linux/07/11/06/0223211.shtml

Also for more info
http://www.openhandsetalliance.com/press_releases.html
http://www.openhandsetalliance.com/press_110507.html
http://googleblog.blogspot.com/2007/11/wheres-my-gphone.html
http://googlesystem.blogspot.com/search/label/Google%20Phone
http://googlesystem.blogspot.com/2007/09/10-questions-about-google-phone.html
http://hardware.slashdot.org/article.pl?sid=07/11/05/139210&from=rss
http://www.pcworld.com/article/id,139293-c,pdacellphonehybrids/article.html
http://www.hindustantimes.com/StoryPage/StoryPage.aspx?id=e2c539e8-524a-418f-aee2-22578a0f6b65&&Headline=Bharti+to+partner+Google+Phone

http://www.openhandsetalliance.com/android_overview.htm

Interesting stuff !!!
Now I just want to know who will win ???
Qutopia , Open Moko , Moblin or Andriod ???

I think FOSS will win !!!

good stuff balanchadar. a few suggestions:

a) am quite uncomfortable about using an 'anon' quote. what if 'anon'
one day steps forward, no longer anonymous, and claims some copyright
or moral rights over the quote? or what if the anon quote had a
totally different context? why can't we just be original.

b) am therefore suggesting a new slogan. from my interactions with all
my wonderful friends in chennai, i feel this may just resonate with
all of us and has a indic flavour in its thought:
"True Knowledge Brings Freedom."

c) the logo needs improvement. it is merely text, and is dependent on
the use of color. also, is the name final?

d) shouldn't the sentence read "ILUGC & NRCFOSS Present"? note the
singular 'present', even though i understand you wish to use an
ampersand. janani could perhaps correct this.

:-)
niyam bhushan

> updated version
> http://dev.balachandar.net/images/foss08v2.jpg

Looks nice!

Some suggestions:

a) If space allows, I suggest changing the '&' to 'and' -- technically 
speaking, & is used only for combining designations or two components of the 
same organisation etc. But, that's not a hard and fast rule. So, you can 
retain '&' is you so wish.

b) It should be 'Present' and not 'Presents'

c) I agree with what Niyam has pointed out -- that using an anonymous quote 
as the sub-caption could lead to copyright issues. So, perhaps we could use 
what Niyam da suggested if the others like it too.

Plus, if you need any text (perhaps notifications or whatever) edited for 
language, I will be more than happy to help.

Warm regards,
Janani

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Wed Nov  7 11:04:16 2007
From: lawgon at thenilgiris.com (Kenneth Gonsalves)
Date: Wed Nov  7 11:04:21 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [Ann] FossConf Chennai feb08 is on
Message-ID: <B97181A9-1AE1-4FD6-B360-5D511D329854@thenilgiris.com>

hi

We have decided on the name: FossConf. The name will be in three parts:

Name: FossConf
City: Chennai (this time)
Date: feb08 (this time)

This leaves us a choice whether to hold it once a year or twice a  
year, and also to change the city each time. The city and date for  
the next FossConf will be announced at the end of the previous  
FossConf. However, regardless of where and when it is held, the scope  
of the conference - newcomers to foss, new speakers, new contributors  
- in short 'Foss for the common man', will not change. So now we move  
to stage two - publicity and getting the common man to come to our  
conference - ideas/action please

Please forward this info to other lists
-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/

Amit Karpe wrote:
> Interesting stuff !!!
> Now I just want to know who will win ???
> Qutopia , Open Moko , Moblin or Andriod ???
>   

iPhone :P. The reason is simple - people don't go out and buy a 
platform, they want a phone that rocks. Of course, a foss-phone is cool, 
but I think an open mobile platform won't take off for the same reason 
that desktop Linux didn't take off - regular people just don't care. 
They simply want something that looks nice and works well enough. For a 
more irreverent take on this, refer to what Fake Steve Jobs has to say :

http://fakesteve.blogspot.com/2007/11/its-not-phone-its-alliance.html

V.

P.S: Warning - some of the folks here might find FSJ's blog close to 
offensive - he calls us "freetards" :D.

completely outdated packages in stable, while ubuntu has a six month release
cycle, more or less, and as far as I can see, a reasonable correspondence to

suresh@frodo 22:44:55 <~> $ cat /etc/debian_version
lenny/sid

>         Again, this is subjective.  I find they make Ubuntu _less_ user
>  friendly, by restricting choices and making choices for the user. I
>  gave up trying to configure Ubuntu for my machine; and ended up by
>  wiping it out and going back to Debian. Not that the task was
>  impossible; it just took too much work to undo all the choices made.

Yes, and in my case I had to rescue my exim config from debconf - either on
debian or on ubuntu - and stick it all in one monolithic file the way exim
originally works.

I would probably spend time doing that for a few other things too, rather
than have the configs, spoolfiles etc scattered all over the filesystem,
quite frequently in entirely non default places that are totally debian
specific. Just not bothered to do so yet.

Which then results in debian specific mailing lists for various pieces of
software (such as exim) getting created after exim-users@exim.org got
cluttered with debian users asking entirely debian specific config
questions, referencing debian specific config variables,  that nobody other
than debian users could answer. Irritating to say the least.

	srs

helpful from emacs wiki.

such add ons , few of which are already a part of emacs.

From vijaykumar at bravegnu.org  Sat Nov 10 10:08:56 2007
From: vijaykumar at bravegnu.org (Vijay Kumar)
Date: Sat Nov 10 10:09:07 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] adding brackets in emacs
In-Reply-To: <BFD1343B-138F-488B-B22E-47F98C6F8D85@thenilgiris.com>
References: <BFD1343B-138F-488B-B22E-47F98C6F8D85@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <473535E0.9040305@bravegnu.org>

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> a common task is adding strings for i18n. Say I have a string - 
> mystring. I need to mark it like so:
> 
> _("mystring").  What I want to do is: select the string and press a key 
> so it will mark it. How is this done in emacs?

The following elisp function will mark the string under cursor with 
_(...). It will not work for one special case in which there is a double 
quotes within the string.

(defun mark-i18n ()
   (interactive)
   (save-excursion
     (search-backward "\"")
     (insert "_(")
     (forward-char 1)
     (search-forward "\"")
     (insert ")")))


Put this definition in your .emacs and bind the function to the key of 
your choice.

Regards,
Vijay

something else, especially in Chennai. Otherwise it doesn't closely
relate to the "rising sun" or "the hand" symbol used be the political

African tribes to use left hand shake to denote that the wish comes
from the heart (which is also adopted in the Scout movement). Its we
Indians who associate left hand with something else and consider it yuck.

From rmathews at gmail.com  Sat Nov 10 12:30:23 2007
From: rmathews at gmail.com (Roshan Mathews)
Date: Sat Nov 10 12:30:33 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] adding brackets in emacs
In-Reply-To: <BFD1343B-138F-488B-B22E-47F98C6F8D85@thenilgiris.com>
References: <BFD1343B-138F-488B-B22E-47F98C6F8D85@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <1c4dc2780711092300k43b18f79u6345ff7382dc3ef@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/10/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
> a common task is adding strings for i18n. Say I have a string -
> mystring. I need to mark it like so:
>
> _("mystring").  What I want to do is: select the string and press a
> key so it will mark it. How is this done in emacs?
>
Hmmm ... I'm assuming you have the string in a buffer/file and need to
convert it from:
  foo
to:
 _("foo")

You can use keyboard macros for this.  Unless you are going to be
using this often, in which case you can use the function given.

C-x (   start defining the macro
C-x )   stop defining
C-x e  to use it
M-x apply-macro-to-region-lines  ...

-- 
Roshan Mathews

On Nov 9, 2007 9:30 PM, srikrishna das <srikrishna_innovations@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hey,
>
> Looks good.
> Inspired from Openmoko?
>
> Hope the android SDK is made available Free (of Cost)
>
 I wouldnt say inspired since rumours of something from google have
been floating around for a long time. It would be interesting since it
will feature Java extensively in its stack. Infact there was even a
rumour that gphone will have openmoko for its software part. Which of
course turned out to be false, since android is a software platform
which other manufacturers can use in their devices, much like
openmoko. Another thing is the apache license associated with it (whch
is GPL2.0 incompatible?). IMO, some GPL compatible license would have
been wonderful which would have provided smooth sharing of code
between the "linux phone platforms", openmoko, moblin et all.
I am also wondering about the degree of openness of the devices
running android, it would be quite cool if you could hack around and
make them run openmoko or moblin.
All in all fun times ahead,

Regards
Sudharshan S

From linuxlingam at gmail.com  Sat Nov 10 18:00:22 2007
From: linuxlingam at gmail.com (Linux Lingam)
Date: Sat Nov 10 18:00:36 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: FossConf new logo suggestion by Niyam
Message-ID: <68ddcb070711100430l62b9de9en20adc801cedde1e@mail.gmail.com>

niyam says:
>a new logo suggestion for fossconf:
>http://www.flickr.com/photos/40299872@N00/1938577522/

kenneth says:
>looks good - but, given the state of politics in TN, it may not be
>wise to use it
[snip + concatenate]
>black and red - dravidian party colours
>rising sun - dmk symbol
>hand - congress symbol
>left hand - yuck
>too risky, in my opinion

[snip + concatenate]

>but it is real good - so if we leave out the explanation, no one will
>make the connection. If we mention rising sun in the explanation ...


hahahahahahhaah! kenneth, you are such a delight! must remember to hug
you when i meet you!
your thinking startles me and makes me ponder on how color and
symbolism are interpreted further. inspired by you will add another 2
or 3 pages to my book 'the art of logo design' once the creativedot
site is up.

meanwhile, to address each point:

black & red is also used by airtel, and not just thousands, but
millions of brands. this because red creates a high neuro-cognitive
response in the human eye, when in contrast with black. so no, that
combination cannot be owned by any one political party, or corporate
brand, or spiritual movement, or whatever. it is universal and
popular.
for instance, it is the color combination of goddess kali, and revered
in west bengal especially.
in some countries, using the same color combination for a
*directly-competing brand* in the *same market* may be a violation.
but lemme see, so far, no other foss event in chennai or india uses
red, black, white. so we're ok. in fact, splendid!

o'reilly uses black red white for their branding, but it is distinctly
different from ours.
their event, which is oscon, uses blue and white.
again, we're distinct and different. no overlaps.

heck, both linuxasia and freed.in use black, orange, and white, and
there are no legal, moral, ethical, or any other issues about it. the
two are still very distinct. EFY also supported the event.


therefore, we can use it, as we are not trying in anyway to evoke any
other party or individual that may use that combination, directly or
indirectly in our symbolism.

then, the hand. congress? blimey! no way! the hand belongs to, well, humans!

i just found 12,300,000 results from the image-search of google for 'hand logo'
please take a look here:
http://images.google.co.in/images?hl=en&q=hand+logo&btnG=Search+Images&gbv=2

please note how the hand is also a universal symbol. again, i can only
think of the mudras depicted on buddha's statues, when i think of the
hand as a symbol.
puting the red-dot on the open hand is exactly for the reasons i
mention in the description: bharatanatyam allusion for tamil nadu's
cultural sharing with the world + openness expressed in an open hand.

incidentally, while researching on bharatanatyam for this logo design,
i learnt with joy that bharatanatyam takes multiple mudras and
gestures, combining or adapting them, to further express more ideas.
so the open hand with a red dot is just to express the ideas mentioned above.

rising sun:
japan, tibet, holiday resorts from around the world, diverse business
brands, creative movements . . .

kenneth, i urge  you to click on the link below. this is my google
search for image-results, for the key word 'rising sun logo'. i found
168,000 results
http://images.google.co.in/images?gbv=2&svnum=10&hl=en&q=rising+sun+logo&btnG=Search+Images

please note quite a few of them are also using red and black in their
color combinations.
so again, our logo is not politically-charged, but culturally,
symbolically, to capture the essence of the foss movement in tamil
nadu. in a sub-continent blessed with abundant sunshine.

left-hand:
bharatanatyam uses both hands, for a sacred and creative purpose. i
allude to that in my logo.
the logo initially had a right-hand, then i flipped it to smile at the
visual pun on 'copy-left'
again, everything goes with out ideas and values of foss.
copy-left is not yuck, but awesome! :-)
i can give a whole researched talk on the importance and understanding
of the left-hand, off-topic, over a nice cup of south indian filter
coffee, some sunny day.

s krishna das wrote:
>Open hand idea is good.
>The perfect circle was itching me
>I made it ellipse.
http://www.geocities.com/srikrishna_innovations/fossconf.in_ellipse.jpg

hmmm ok, looks good too, but i'd like to stick to a perfect circle for
the following reasons:

a) bharatanatyam uses a perfect circle, though hand-drawn. here is my reference:
http://www.noopur.com/students.html

b) in bharatanatyam they also paint the finger tips red. i tried that
with the logo, but it looked too garish and harsh as the logo is well,
a logo, and not a photograph. so dropped it to just fingers/digits,
and the perfect circle.

c) the perfect circle also evokes the CD, DVD, and disc media.

d) works for the rising sun imagery.

e) contrast visually, of the perfection of the circle to the rough
organic brush strokes of the fingers/digits.

even then, i am okay with the use of an ellipse circle if all of you
strongly prefer an ellipse.


finally, use of other colors:
have noted in events, a lot of the collateral is screen-printed, such
as teeshirts, some banners, etc. every color adds to the cost. so i
decided to stick to one color (red) plus black. the typical background
color for the use of this logo would be black, white, grey, or even
any other color. it adapts perfectly well for that.
as kenneth notes, the red is not exactly pure-red, but a slightly orangish-red.
i could also change it to another tone of red, the hex values are: ff334cff

this is the tone i find that matches the tone of red used in bharatanatyam.

just tried it in the logo, looks good. my only worry is that getting
it to match in digital prints, teeshirt prints, etc will take some
effort at your end. but hey! we can live with that. :-)
here's the logo with the new red tone:

http://www.flickr.com/photos/40299872@N00/1946471801/


i must share with all of you that i spent a considerable number of
hours trying to find a unique mudra to draw as the logo. however, at
low-resolutions, at small sizes, the mudra becomes quite squished.
plus, each mudra in bharatanatyam conveys a variety of meanings. i
found the 'mukula' mudra the most suitable as it signifies 'bud'.
further research showed this mudra combines or adapts to form several
other meanings as well.

the open-hand mudra just conveys everything, and most importantly,
scales to form a distinct favicon in your browser. a logo that can
scale to such a small size is a pearl in an oyster. :-)


over to you guys!
hope you finalize in a day or two,
then will find time and create the banner for the websites.

please share: what is the slogan of the event?
i remember taking part in this discussion a week ago, but do not know
if this got resolved.
had recommended a slogan as well.

finally, will later add the details of the typography of the logotype as well.

:-)
niyam bhushan

On 11/10/07, Sudharshan S <sudharsh@gmail.com> wrote:

>  I wouldnt say inspired since rumours of something from google have
> been floating around for a long time. It would be interesting since it
> will feature Java extensively in its stack. Infact there was even a
> rumour that gphone will have openmoko for its software part. Which of
> course turned out to be false, since android is a software platform
> which other manufacturers can use in their devices, much like
> openmoko. Another thing is the apache license associated with it (whch

 I think they are going to use _standard_ devices and not going to
manufacture the devices. So, it should be posible to run any
openembedded based distro on these devices. You can start trying it
today itself instead of waiting for Android platform to be released.
 Moreover, if this idea succeeds it can turn out to be turning out to
be a turning point for the indutry. First of all Google has announced
that the software stack will be under APL. Secondly instead of
creating there _own_ mobile handset, _own_ mobile distro and another
ecosystem, Google is creating a consortium of manufactures, service
providers and software companies. Such a consortium, if works out,
will definatley be benificial for the consumer as well as small to
medium sized players.
 So lets see what comes out. May be we are looking at the unification
of mobile industry ?

regards
VK

> a logo, and not a photograph. so dropped it to just fingers/digits,
> and the perfect circle.
>
> c) the perfect circle also evokes the CD, DVD, and disc media.
>
> d) works for the rising sun imagery.
>
> e) contrast visually, of the perfection of the circle to the rough
> organic brush strokes of the fingers/digits.
>
> even then, i am okay with the use of an ellipse circle if all of you
> strongly prefer an ellipse.
>
>
> finally, use of other colors:
> have noted in events, a lot of the collateral is screen-printed, such
> as teeshirts, some banners, etc. every color adds to the cost. so i
> decided to stick to one color (red) plus black. the typical background
> color for the use of this logo would be black, white, grey, or even
> any other color. it adapts perfectly well for that.
> as kenneth notes, the red is not exactly pure-red, but a slightly  
> orangish-red.
> i could also change it to another tone of red, the hex values are:  
> ff334cff
>
> this is the tone i find that matches the tone of red used in  
> bharatanatyam.
>
> just tried it in the logo, looks good. my only worry is that getting
> it to match in digital prints, teeshirt prints, etc will take some
> effort at your end. but hey! we can live with that. :-)
> here's the logo with the new red tone:
>
> http://www.flickr.com/photos/40299872@N00/1946471801/
>
>
> i must share with all of you that i spent a considerable number of
> hours trying to find a unique mudra to draw as the logo. however, at
> low-resolutions, at small sizes, the mudra becomes quite squished.
> plus, each mudra in bharatanatyam conveys a variety of meanings. i
> found the 'mukula' mudra the most suitable as it signifies 'bud'.
> further research showed this mudra combines or adapts to form several
> other meanings as well.
>
> the open-hand mudra just conveys everything, and most importantly,
> scales to form a distinct favicon in your browser. a logo that can
> scale to such a small size is a pearl in an oyster. :-)
>
>
> over to you guys!
> hope you finalize in a day or two,
> then will find time and create the banner for the websites.
>
> please share: what is the slogan of the event?
> i remember taking part in this discussion a week ago, but do not know
> if this got resolved.
> had recommended a slogan as well.
>
> finally, will later add the details of the typography of the  
> logotype as well.

I know I'm so late in joining this discussion (which is probably closed 
already). And I also saw a lot of emails in this thread (which I didn't read 
because I wanted to see the logo through my eyes without any explanations, 
which is how anybody outside of this mailing list will see it), and here is 
what I saw...

(a) Left palm with the marudhaani dot in the centre. Very indigenous. Nice.
(b) Rising sun (but very low risk of being mixed with DMK symbol as the dot 
is organish).
(c) A bharathanatyam symbol which (to my layman knowledge) means both stop, 
as well as 'be calm, I am there' (reassuring)
(d) A longish ring finger, which (going by the cliche) means somebody 
skilled in the arts.
(e) Slender fingers usually characterises those who work hard.

I understand the left hand was chosen to link this with copyleft, but I so 
wish this were the right hand, because an open right hand signifies somebody 
who is happy to give.

Cheers,
Janani

On 18:49:37 Nov 11, Peter Boosten wrote:
> Thanks for your answer, although that's not quite what I'm looking for:
> 

Okay. Find my answer below.

> I know it's possible to 'shape' the traffic with altq, so it's possible in
> theory to shape certain kind of traffic to almost nihil. Smart devices
> like packetshapers (and even some proxy appliances like Blue Coat) have
> separate categories for streaming media, so I was wondering if PF and altq
> could do the same.

Well I have no idea about appliances or commercial software. 

I can however tell you what I know. I have never tried these things but
I can tell you what I have understood.

First and foremost you can only shape outgoing traffic. You cannot do
QoS with incoming traffic. You might be able to manipulate things a
little but you have far more power when it comes to deciding how you
want others to receive packets from you.

This is the basic idea. You can only do traffic shaping with egress
traffic. Not with ingress traffic.

Now, pf + altq can do very sophisticated traffic shaping.

There are three categories of queuing disciples supported by pf.

a ) class based queuing (cbq)

b ) priority based queuing (priq)

c ) hierarchical fair service curve (hfsc)

Each of these mechanisms have pros and cons and you have to pick one of
them based on your requirements.

The configuration for basic QoS management consists of three steps.

1) The altq statement ( which interface to work on , how much bandwidth
you want to play around with and also the queuing discipline (one of
the above)

2) You have to define the "queue" rules to determine how the total
bandwidth in the above line has to be split amongst the various
categories. Typically they are split into multiple queues based on port
numbers but other possibilities also exist. For instance you will want
to allocate bulk of the bandwidth for important mail traffic and
browsing but you want to restrict p2p and other protocols. It is the
"queue" lines that also determine what to do when there is congestion. 
 (IOW most of the tweaking happens here :)

3) Next step is to use the pf filter rules to allocate which queues to
use for handling which traffic

I shall illustrate with an example. This is not my own. I am taking it
from the pf man page.

  1)  altq on dc0 cbq bandwidth 5Mb queue { std, http, mail, ssh }

  2) queue std bandwidth 10% cbq(default)
     queue http bandwidth 60% priority 2 cbq(borrow red) \
           { employees, developers }
     queue  developers bandwidth 75% cbq(borrow)
     queue  employees bandwidth 15%
     queue mail bandwidth 10% priority 0 cbq(borrow ecn)
     queue ssh bandwidth 20% cbq(borrow) { ssh_interactive, ssh_bulk }
     queue  ssh_interactive bandwidth 50% priority 7 cbq(borrow)
     queue  ssh_bulk bandwidth 50% priority 0 cbq(borrow)

 3)  block return out on dc0 inet all queue std
     pass out on dc0 inet proto tcp from $developerhosts to any port 80
\
           keep state queue developers
     pass out on dc0 inet proto tcp from $employeehosts to any port 80 \
           keep state queue employees
     pass out on dc0 inet proto tcp from any to any port 22 \
           keep state queue(ssh_bulk, ssh_interactive)
     pass out on dc0 inet proto tcp from any to any port 25 \
           keep state queue mail

As you can see the first line is the altq directive. You have defined a
list of queues (std, http, mail, ssh) and also mentioned that you want
to use class based queuing.

Then the queue rules determine how individual queues should share the
bandwidth amongst themselves. But we are not quite done yet.

The most critical step is the filter rules that determine when to queue
traffic and which queue to assign to.

That happens in 3). 

It should be self explanatory.

Please note that we have used "pass out" which corresponds to my main
idea of determining how traffic leaves our network.

Once data arrives on the interface, it is already too late to do QoS
manipulation.

This is not completely true (you can do bandwidth throttling) but at
least relatively speaking this idea appears to be correct.

> 
> Your solution works, however you'll have to know what sites are being
> visited in order to block them entirely.
> 

Hope the above explanation suffices.

Can you clarify your needs a bit more?

Thanks.

Best,
Girish

Dear All,

 

We are looking into the EHCI driver source code in Linux kernel 2.6.14 version. Actually we want to know the function flow at the time of the device connection (i.e. at the time of enumeration phase). For this, we built the Linux image by including the debug statements through printks in EHCI related files in Linux source code (drivers/usb/host). We found that the ehci_start callback method is invoked from usb_hcd_pci_probe method at the time of initialization (when we run modprobe / insmod command). The same we tried to know the name of the method which invokes the ehci_urb_enqueue callback method of the EHCI. We have noticed the following function flow in the /var/log/messages file / through dmesg command after inserting the device into a USB port.

 

ehci_urb_enqueue?qh_urb_transaction ? qtd_fill

   ?submit async ? qtd_append_tds

   ? qh_link_async.

 

We have also noticed that qh_link_async moves filled qheads into asynchronous list  by writing  the command into the EHCI operational register's command register. 

 

We are not able to find the function name that which invokes the ehci_urb_enqueue method. So, could any one please tell/suggest us the function name OR procedure to find out. 

 

Thanks and Regards,

Srinivas G

From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Nov 12 17:05:03 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Function flow at the time of USB device connection
	(Enumeration)
In-Reply-To: <15C2CAD382CB69409395ED4F159BED7050EFE9@mail.esntechnologies.co.in>
References: <15C2CAD382CB69409395ED4F159BED7050EFE9@mail.esntechnologies.co.in>

Hi,

----- On 11/12/07, Srinivas G. <srinivasg@esntechnologies.co.in> wrote:
| ehci_urb_enqueue method. So, could any one please tell/suggest us the
| function name OR procedure to find out.
\--

1. What is your platform?

2. Learn to use lxr.linux.no:

http://lxr.linux.no/ident?i=ehci_urb_enqueue

Depending on the bus to which the host controller is connected, the
corresponding functions are registered. For example, PCI based (2.6
Linux kernel):

http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/host/ehci-pci.c#L354

Follow:

>From hub, for example invokes usb_submit_urb():
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/hub.c
    |
    v
hcd.c - usb_submit_urb ()
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/urb.c#L220
    |
    v
urb.c - usb_hcd_submit_urb ()
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/urb.c#L375
    |
    v
core/hcd.c - hcd->driver->urb_enqueue ()
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/hcd.c#L1014

SK

Shakthi Kannan

Hi,

Replying to my own post.

----- On 11/12/07, Shakthi Kannan <shakthimaan@gmail.com> wrote:
| hcd.c - usb_submit_urb ()
| http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/urb.c#L220
\--

Sorry, this should have been:
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/hcd.c#L921

When you connect the device, root hub port status changes, and
generates hub interrupt request, so usb_submit_urb() should have been
invoked from hub_irq():

hub.c - hub_irq()
http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/usb/core/hub.c#L338

SK

Shakthi Kannan

here's the fstab entry:
/dev/sda2 /media/Media vfat rw,user,sync 0 3

(my / and /home, both reiserfs, are mounted 1,2)

/media/Media has 3 directories:
Downloads, My\ Music, Videos

In my /home/lvshankar I have 3 sym links to the above 3 directories.

without -o ) or when after the systems boots (which runs mount -a, i guess),
I am not able to write/delete anything in the newly mounted filesystem.
But, when I (re)mount through GParted (right click on /dev/sda2 and say
mount), I am having proper rights. And the owner is show as my user
(lvshankar) account too.

Can anyone help me? And what is GParted exactly doing?

# /etc/fstab: static file system information.
#

/dev/cdrom /media/cdrom0 udf,iso9660 user,noauto 0 0

Add 'noauto' and 'users' to your fstab entry.
And if dbus/hal is running, your favourite file manager should automatically mount the storage device with rw permissions
for normal users.
If you want to manually mount the device, check out 'pmount' .

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Nov 13 11:56:14 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Nov 13 11:57:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] LJ Tip: SuperCat
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0711131152390.1017-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

LJ Tip: Supercat Text Colorizer

The application Supercat colors any input text based on the type of
file and a set of rules associated with the file type. The rules are
used to match strings found in the input text and can be specified
using simple characters or strings, regular expressions and special
time-formatting rules. Supercat is flexible and extensible; new file
types can be added without software development.

You can download Supercat (at the time of writing the latest version
was 0.5.3) at http://supercat.nosredna.net. Supercat is also available
in Gentoo's portage system and Ubuntu's to-be-released Hardy Heron.
Installing Supercat is fairly straightforward -- the only thing you
need to specify is the --system-directory 'configure' option. Once
installed, you can run Supercat on numerous files. For example:

$> spc file.c

This presents you with a colorized listing (similar to how Vim colors
text). Supercat tries to figure out the file type based on the file
suffix or, in the case of files with the extension .log, Supercat
removes the suffix and looks up the file name (e.g., error.log is file
type error). The user can explicitly override the file type on the
command line.

All rules for colorizing text are stored in files with names of the
form spcrc-ext, where "ext" is the file type. These files are stored
in the configured "system directory" or else your private ~/.spcrc
directory.

All rules for colorizing text are stored in files with names of the
form spcrc-ext, where "ext" is the file type. These files are stored
in the configured "system directory" or else your private ~/.spcrc
directory. For example, the rules for a C source code file in spcrc-c
might look like:

# HTML COL COL A N T CHARACTER, STRING or REGULAR EXPRESSION
########## ### # # # #############################################
Red        red b     ([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)[[:space:]]*(
Yellow     yel b     (while|for|if|switch|main|return)[[:space:]]*(
Yellow     yel b   s else
Cyan       cya     s case
Cyan       cya     s return
Cyan       cya     s default
Cyan       cya b     [[:space:]]*(include)
Green      grn       (do)[[:space:]]*{
Green      grn       (break|continue)[[:space:]]*;
Magenta    mag       (int|char|short|float|double|long|unsigned)[[:space:]]
Blue       blu b     [^[:alnum:]_]([[:digit:]]+)
Yellow     yel       "(.*)"
Yellow     yel       <(.*)>
Magenta    mag     c :;

Matching is performed using the information in the pattern at the end
of each line in the configuration file. If a portion of a line matches
the pattern then the matching characters are given the specified
color. The type of matching is specified in the 'T' column and
defaults to REGEXP.

The other columns specify the video coloring attributes to the used.
"COL" indicates the console color; "A" is an optional video attributes
(e.g., bold, underline); "N" governs the number of times a match is
applied to a line. The "HTML COL" column is there because Supercat
supports outputting its colorized text in HTML format for viewing with
a Web browser.

Supercat provides flexibility and extensibility without requiring
programming. There are numerous other options and goodies that
Supercat has to offer, but I'll let you find them as they are
extensive and out of the scope of this short HOWTO.

--
Bharathi S

From yogeshk at redim.net  Tue Nov 13 12:43:22 2007
From: yogeshk at redim.net (Yogesh Kumar K)
Date: Tue Nov 13 12:43:20 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] convert dynamic link to static link using GCC compile for
	C++
Message-ID: <20071113071322.161280dc@mail.redim.net>

hi,

in my project i need to create the executable file in the static library file to be share instead of dynamic , 
i made the changes of code as follows 


  make file content is before change
  ************************
  
g++ -c -O0 -g -pthread -DCASINO_TWIST  -DTARGET_UNIX -DTARGET_LINUX -DMYSQL4 -I.. -I../src -I../lib  -I/usr/include/mysql -o ../lib/sql/mMySQL.o ../lib/sql/mMySQL.cpp
  g++ -c -O0 -g -pthread -DCASINO_TWIST  -DTARGET_UNIX -DTARGET_LINUX -DMYSQL4 -I.. -I../src -I../lib  -I/usr/include/mysql -o ../lib/thread/m_thread.o  ../lib/thread/m_thread.cpp
  
make file content is after change
************************
g++ -static -static-libgcc -c -O0 -g -pthread -DCASINO_TWIST -DTARGET_UNIX -DTARGET_LINUX -DMYSQL4 -I.. -I../src -I../lib -I/usr/include/mysql -o ../lib/sql/mMySQL.o ../lib/sql/mMySQL.cpp
g++ -static -static-libgcc -c -O0 -g -pthread -DCASINO_TWIST -DTARGET_UNIX -DTARGET_LINUX -DMYSQL4 -I.. -I../src -I../lib -I/usr/include/mysql -o ../lib/thread/m_thread.o ../lib/thread/m_thread.cpp


[root@redhat unix]# make -f Makefile_server_twistcasino

From solar345 at gmail.com  Tue Nov 13 15:40:20 2007
From: solar345 at gmail.com (Antano Solar)
Date: Tue Nov 13 15:40:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Unethical IT company - NetDomains
Message-ID: <b2600ec40711130210l66364e5fue44b9113933c0ab9@mail.gmail.com>

Hi ,

This is to share my experience with a company called netdomains near guindy
run by Mr.Santhosh.

It is written with just the intention to help the open source developers not
get fooled into certain work practises .

I joined this company as a consultant. It had nothing to call  its business
except for a 3rd party service which they were buying and selling , a
designr who knows html  , no css and no javascrit and one .net developer for
small web contracts that they take.

I was assigned the job to complete 4 projects.

1. Train a new recruit fresher with no idea of opensource  , not any  mvc
framework , no javascript  to make a personal information manager with the
feel of outlook express online.

2.Developement of a control panel which is more user friendly and fully
functional as cpanel from scratch.

3.Develop a website builder

4.Develop a system where all the above integrates.

And besides that , help the .net developer with every doubt that he gets
stuck at.
Make technical documentation(proposal) for new contracts the company
pursues.
Provide solutions for every small project they pursue.

Lots of work . And it was clearly mentioned each one will be done
consequtively.

I was on a payroll.

First month he pays me half of the money and says in few days he will pay
the rest as he is financially week.

Second month , not even half the money.

Then he bring a sorry state and gets me to work without payment for the
remaining months.

The developer whom he recruitted quits  , leaving PIM half way.
She was paid 3000 a month obvious she will quit once she got the knowledge.

Sales guy quits

Front desk lady quits

.net developer quits

I rebuke the .net developer ,asking how can he be so unethical to quit
without prior notice and proper handover.

He informs that his salary was just 4000 rupees and even that was not paid
regularly.
The same guy now works for 32k a month in a different company.
The same guy brings me to light of the companies former practises , how
before me someone else was doing things and they were not paid too.


A new sales guy was recruited  for 30k a month who quit his job in NIS.

End of the month he is not paid too.

When I ask my payment , the man says I am expensive for him .
So he would like to put development  on hold till things turn good.

Then after 1 week he makes a peanut 5k payment and says you have to help us
finsinh the projects , so that we can pay your pending amounts.

Now he wants me to help him for free , not even as debit .. for me to get my
pending payments.

Out of pure pity I accept to dedicate 4 hours every week to just give
guidance to his new recruit  developer for free.
He  sends a statement saying he owes me 75k and wil be paid soon.

After 1 week , he calls me and says something has to be done to develop
things.

I tell him , anymore support from me would require payment in advance .

He currently mails me saying that I dont deserve the money and I need
to complete the above mentioned projets to get payment.

I was  on  a payroll .
Few of the projects were done more than once and totally scrapped off ,
becasue he came up with totally new requirments.

I have an agreement signed by him before I joined work.

Should I pass it on to my family lawers is still something I am speculating
on.



Moral of the story:

1. When on payroll and a salary is not paid in full on the appointed date -
QUIT. th first month.

2. Kindly consider and get payments in advance for your own good before
doing anything for netdomains.


Antano Solar John

Hi,

----- On 11/13/07, Srinivas G. <srinivasg@esntechnologies.co.in> wrote:
| We are using the Linux 2.6.14 version.
\--

That is Linux kernel version. By platform, I meant target platform -
ARM/x86/ppc/sparc/et. al.

-----
| We did not find the 2.6.14 version cross reference at the above link.
\--

Well, you can setup lxr locally on your 2.6.14 code base.
http://sourceforge.net/projects/lxr

-----
| By the way, please let us know the procedure for
| building the ehci-hcd.ko file whenever there is a modification
| to the files existing in the USB/CORE directory.
\--

If you enable them as module (M) in the kernel config, simply doing
make in the kernel sources will re-build them, and you can transfer
just the modules on the target platform, and test them.

If you make them built-in to the kernel, you will need to re-install
the kernel, and use it during every test.

Regards,

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From: ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in [mailto:ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in] On
Behalf Of Antano Solar
Sent: Tuesday, November 13, 2007 3:40 PM
To: ILUG-C
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Unethical IT company - NetDomains

Hi ,

This is to share my experience with a company called netdomains near guindy
run by Mr.Santhosh.

It is written with just the intention to help the open source developers not
get fooled into certain work practises .

I joined this company as a consultant. It had nothing to call  its business
except for a 3rd party service which they were buying and selling , a
designr who knows html  , no css and no javascrit and one .net developer for
small web contracts that they take.

I was assigned the job to complete 4 projects.

1. Train a new recruit fresher with no idea of opensource  , not any  mvc
framework , no javascript  to make a personal information manager with the
feel of outlook express online.

2.Developement of a control panel which is more user friendly and fully
functional as cpanel from scratch.

3.Develop a website builder

4.Develop a system where all the above integrates.

And besides that , help the .net developer with every doubt that he gets
stuck at.
Make technical documentation(proposal) for new contracts the company
pursues.
Provide solutions for every small project they pursue.

Lots of work . And it was clearly mentioned each one will be done
consequtively.

I was on a payroll.

First month he pays me half of the money and says in few days he will pay
the rest as he is financially week.

Second month , not even half the money.

Then he bring a sorry state and gets me to work without payment for the
remaining months.

The developer whom he recruitted quits  , leaving PIM half way.
She was paid 3000 a month obvious she will quit once she got the knowledge.

Sales guy quits

Front desk lady quits

.net developer quits

I rebuke the .net developer ,asking how can he be so unethical to quit
without prior notice and proper handover.

He informs that his salary was just 4000 rupees and even that was not paid
regularly.
The same guy now works for 32k a month in a different company.
The same guy brings me to light of the companies former practises , how
before me someone else was doing things and they were not paid too.


A new sales guy was recruited  for 30k a month who quit his job in NIS.

End of the month he is not paid too.

When I ask my payment , the man says I am expensive for him .
So he would like to put development  on hold till things turn good.

Then after 1 week he makes a peanut 5k payment and says you have to help us
finsinh the projects , so that we can pay your pending amounts.

Now he wants me to help him for free , not even as debit .. for me to get my
pending payments.

Out of pure pity I accept to dedicate 4 hours every week to just give
guidance to his new recruit  developer for free.
He  sends a statement saying he owes me 75k and wil be paid soon.

After 1 week , he calls me and says something has to be done to develop
things.

I tell him , anymore support from me would require payment in advance .

He currently mails me saying that I dont deserve the money and I need to
complete the above mentioned projets to get payment.

I was  on  a payroll .
Few of the projects were done more than once and totally scrapped off ,
becasue he came up with totally new requirments.

I have an agreement signed by him before I joined work.

Should I pass it on to my family lawers is still something I am speculating
on.



Moral of the story:

1. When on payroll and a salary is not paid in full on the appointed date -
QUIT. th first month.

2. Kindly consider and get payments in advance for your own good before
doing anything for netdomains.


Antano Solar John

From niraj at efyindia.com  Tue Nov 13 21:05:35 2007
From: niraj at efyindia.com (Niraj Sahay)
Date: Tue Nov 13 21:07:18 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [Commercial] Why not enroll in FOSS India Awards?
Message-ID: <4739C447.6030700@efyindia.com>

Hi,

Are you working on any free software or open source (FOSS) project? Do 
you know anyone who is?

There's a great opportunity for all Indian FOSS contributors to showcase 
their work at the national level, and perhaps global too! Plus, the 
development team (or individual) can get a minimum cash prize of Rs 25,000!

But, there's more to it than just cash prize. The winners will get 
exclusive coverage in LINUX For You magazine, and openITis.com (aka 
linuxforu.com). Which in turn could mean: (a) more media coverage for 
the project and its developers, (b) publicity amongst targeted 
customers, and (c) more contributors getting attracted to the project.

Launched with an initial kitty of Rs 5 lakhs, the FOSS India Awards aim 
to recognise India's top 20 FOSS projects. The LINUX For You team is 
working with FOSII (Forum for Open Source Initiatives in India) on this 
venture.

The registration for FOSS India Awards is FREE! All one has to do to 
register is to visit http://www.openitis.com/awards/ and fill in the 
two-minute form. Registration for FOSS India Awards is open till 15th 
December '07. The awards will be announced during Open Source India Week 
(aka LinuxAsia 2008) during the 2nd week of February '08.

Please do forward this message to anyone whom you believe is working on 
a FOSS project, and is a good candidate.

Let's prove to the World that India contributes to FOSS too...

Best Wishes!
LINUX For You team

looks ok to me. No harm in having more than one slogan. btw, can the  
thamizh guys please create tamil version of all this?

re copyright. As far as I know, the copyright to a conference logo  
should belong to the conference. Further, it cannot be 'shared' under  
some license as the use of the same should be restricted to  
situations relevant to the conference. That is, the logo can only be  
used for conference publicity materials, and if it is used on any  
website, the same must link back to the conference website.  
Similarly, no one can modify or distribute the logo without approval  
of the copyright owners - and such modification and distribution can  
only be done to further the aims of the conference. As such the only  
possible modifications would be changing the city name and date for  
future conferences or changing the language of the text. You have  
much more experience in these fields, so how would you like to deal  
with this?

On 14-Nov-07, at 8:28 AM, Sriram Karra wrote:

>> Writing is irrelevant (I *am* a lawyer),
>>
>
> alright that really did catch my attention. What exactly do you  
> mean by
> that? Doesn't contract law accept even verbal contract as legally  
> binding?
> (Aren't an offer and acceptance enough to make a contract legally  
> binding?)

it's binding - even if it is not in writing. But in practice, in my  
career as a lawyer, I have almost always advised clients in these  
situations to cut their losses and move on. Take the most common  
contract - you take a newb and make him sign a bond undertaking to  
work for at least two years after his training is over or forfeit  
some sum of money. He gets trained and scoots. What do you do?  
Legally you can sue him - practically speaking its better to cut the  
losses and move on. In the instant case, although the OP has a cast  
iron case, the employer doesnt have the money to pay him. So if he  
sues, the only people who will profit are the lawyers.

By saying that whether the contract is in writing or not is  
irrelevant, I mean that in the last analysis sincerity of the parties  
and their willingness (and ability) to keep to the agreement are far  
more important than mere promises - whether written or oral.

I could not update the contents of the brochure wiki, tried twice and
on both occassions, evan after waiting for ~05 minutes, no updates.

Hence, am posting my changes below. Would someone, kindly update the
wiki accordingly.

==========================================

= FossConf Chennai feb08 =

The Indian Linux Users Group, Chennai Chapter (ILUGC), in association
with NRC-FOSS, Chennai takes great pleasure in inviting you to
participate in the FossConf to be held at MIT, Chromepet, Chennai from
noon on 01 Feb, 2008 to noon on 03 Feb, 2008.

== THE ORGANISERS ==

ILUGC is one of the oldest lugs in the country and has been
continously active since it was founded. It keeps a low profile and
specialises in grass roots work all around TamilNadu (and in the
neighbouring states too). Under it's guidance, many lugs are active in
colleges and towns all around TamilNadu. At the same time, Chennai LUG
members are in the forefront of the FOSS movement both at the national
and international level.

NRC-FOSS, a Central Government Project, funded by the DIT and jointly
run by CDAC and AU-KBC Research Centre, Chennai, for the past two and
half years has been actively promoting FOSS in the academic domain.
It's main focus has been getting FOSS introduced into the curriculum
of Engineering Colleges in the country. Also, apart from encouraging
student projects in FOSS, it has been active in encouraging academia
to release it's work under FOSS/Creative Commons licenses. AU-KBC
Research Centre, MIT, Chennai has strengths in NLP, Bio-informatics,
Wireless, Cryptography and embedded computing, much of which utilizes
FOSS tools and has released some of this research material as FOSS.

== SCOPE ==

The conference will focus on both, new users / contributors to FOSS.
It will help improve their skills and give them experience in speaking
and presenting on their subject.

 * For college lecturers/professors: Training in teaching and
presentation of FOSS subjects
 * For Government employeess: Orientation on how to more effectively
use their GNU/Linux and FOSS based systems
 * For students: Guidance in developing FOSS projects
 * For systems administrators: Orientation in setting up secure,
efficient servers and networks
 * For academic researchers: a new arena to present your research and
contribute back to the people who gave you your FOSS research tools
 * For FOSS developers: a chance to share your knowledge with the new
generation and to interact with your friends around the country

== Programs ==

 * Talks - 45 minutes each on every conceivable foss related topic
 * Mini talks - 10 minutes each, on some aspect of foss
 * Tutorials - upto 2 hours of intense instruction on a particular subject
 * Sprints - groups of people working to achieve some target - coding,
translation, documentation, bug-fixing ...
 * Formal Academic presentations - on research done using foss tools
from the academic community
 * Marathadi talks: informal presentations and discussions under the
trees in the campus
 * Demos: Installation of distros, graphics, games, embedded linux products
 * Student projects: Presentations on student projects using foss.
Ideas for further projects
 * Cultural competitions: Art, poetry, songs, skits

==========================================

/Ram

From vijaykumar at bravegnu.org  Wed Nov 14 13:58:42 2007
From: vijaykumar at bravegnu.org (Vijay Kumar)
Date: Wed Nov 14 13:58:29 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Talk on Qemu
Message-ID: <473AB1BA.7030809@bravegnu.org>

Zilogic Systems is organizing a talk on Qemu. Qemu is an open source 
machine emulator, that can emulate a wide variety of processors (x86, 
ARM, MIPS, PPC to name a few) together with all peripheral devices 
required to build a complete system. The talk will describe how Qemu can 
be used as an environment for learning Linux device driver development. 
The details of the talk are given below.

Topic: Qemu for Kernel Newbies
Speaker: Vijay Kumar
Date: 18th Nov, 07
Time: 4:00pm to 5:00pm
Venue:
Zilogic Systems,
11/15, Ground Floor,
Saroja Apartments,
Fourth Main Road,
Kamaraj Nagar,
Thiruvanmiyur,
Chennai.

A location map to reach the venue is available from 
http://www.zilogic.com/contact.html

All are invited. There is no entry fee.

Regards,
Vijay

Website: http://www.bravegnu.org

>
> it's binding - even if it is not in writing. But in practice, in my
> career as a lawyer, I have almost always advised clients in these
> situations to cut their losses and move on. Take the most common
> contract - you take a newb and make him sign a bond undertaking to
> work for at least two years after his training is over or forfeit
> some sum of money. He gets trained and scoots. What do you do?
> Legally you can sue him - practically speaking its better to cut the
> losses and move on. In the instant case, although the OP has a cast
> iron case, the employer doesnt have the money to pay him. So if he
> sues, the only people who will profit are the lawyers.
>
> By saying that whether the contract is in writing or not is
> irrelevant, I mean that in the last analysis sincerity of the parties
> and their willingness (and ability) to keep to the agreement are far
> more important than mere promises - whether written or oral.
>

I thought  bonds to work for x years are not valid in India.

Anyway for my case , I have my appointment letter and was on payroll and not
on contract and we had one month notification agreement.And I agree with
kenneth that even when you are legally strong, it is at most times not worth
the effort(from the cases that I hear from a few lawyers I know).

Antano Solar John

On 14-Nov-07, at 4:55 PM, Antano Solar wrote:

>>> I thought  bonds to work for x years are not valid in India.
>>
>> they aren't?
>>
>>
> It was valid a while ago , but it is not anymore.

there are two types of bond - one, you join a company and sign a bond  
saying you will work for at least three years - this was never valid

two - join a company where they quantify the training they are going  
to give you and you undertake to work for X years or refund the money  
spent on you - valid. They still cant make you work if you dont want  
to, but they can sue you for the money spent on your training - if  
they can prove they spent it. And prove they trained you.

From m.sujith at gmail.com  Thu Nov 15 00:05:49 2007
From: m.sujith at gmail.com (Sujith Manoharan)
Date: Thu Nov 15 00:06:36 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] problem mounting fat32 partition
In-Reply-To: <72288b670711140740h31fb3410g892318d7acd3c5fa@mail.gmail.com>
References: <72288b670711140740h31fb3410g892318d7acd3c5fa@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071114103549.7d73891b.m.sujith@gmail.com>

On Wed, 14 Nov 2007 21:10:00 +0530
"VidhyaShankar L" <lv.shankar@gmail.com> wrote:
> Thanks. Nautilus automatically mounts the partition when I try to open it.
> But, all my media is in this parition. W/o me mounting it, my audio player
> says
> the file does not exist. I use Amarok. Any suggestions?

You can add a mount command to your autostart file.
A simple 'pmount <dev> MMEDIA' would be sufficient.
The location of the autostart file is dependant on the desktop environment you use.
I am assuming you use KDE - so check in ~/.kde .
If you want an environment agnostic solution, add the mount command to /etc/rc.local .

HTH.

Sujith
-- 
http://m.sujith.googlepages.com

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Fri Nov 16 17:09:50 2007

Subject: [Ilugc] Foss Conf Logo-2

References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0711161700520.3585-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80711160339q92301ne9d77ae8385df7b8@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

----- On 11/16/07, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
| I uploaded my version of logo in the following link:
| http://registration.fossconf.in/code/attachment/wiki/DesignPublicity/logo1.png
\--

First impressions:

1. Not sure who/why they are running, but, on first glance it looks
like a banner for some marathon!

2. Always use sans-serif for headings. Title/headings should not have
styles or features that make it difficult to read.

Imagine a conference poster put-up on the back of a public bus. While
the bus is moving, at first glance, people should be able to grasp as
much info as possible from the poster; not spend time just trying to
decipher the name of the conference.

3. Avoid regional languages, unless it is a focused conference only to
a particular region or group of people. People who don't understand
the phrases may not give in to it easily, or simply won't care.

4. Keep it simple.

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

ahh. You may have noticed a request on this list to translate the  
logo and slogans into tamil. No one has responded to it so far. In my  
opinion, the logo on the website and posters as well as slogans etc  
should be in english for the english version of the site/posters and  
in Tamil for the tamil version. The registration website is  
bilingual. Talks can be in either language, and, if we want to reach  
our target audience, most of the publicity material must also be in  
Tamil. The whole problem is finalising the logo. We thought is was  
finalised, but again apprehensions of physical danger from wearing a  
conference T shirt have been raised, so the logo is still not fully  
finalised. But even then, we need lots of slogans both in English and  
tamil. We need the conference brochure, both in english and tamil -  
none of this work has even been commenced in Tamil though we are well  
on the way with the English versions.

The Mumbai brochure mentioned in ticket: http:// 
registration.fossconf.in/code/ticket/10 is the result of nearly two  
months of hard work balancing the viewpoints of both the OSS people  
and the GNU people, and many people from Chennai participated in  
formulating it. It is an excellent piece of work and needs to be  
urgently translated and made part of the conference publicity  
material. So let's move on

kg

http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/
