> our target audience, most of the publicity material must also be in
> Tamil. The whole problem is finalising the logo. We thought is was
> finalised, but again apprehensions of physical danger from wearing a
> conference T shirt have been raised, so the logo is still not fully
> finalised. But even then, we need lots of slogans both in English and
> tamil. We need the conference brochure, both in english and tamil -
> none of this work has even been commenced in Tamil though we are well

1. Sorry about my outbursts. Yesterday was a long day and I was fed up
with more than one thing :-).

2. I did not take up any responsibilities, for the conference date
directly clashes with the most significant day of the year for the
industry I am involved in.

Since no one has taken up the translation task, I volunteer to
co-ordinate translating all the publicity material into Tamil for the
conference.

3. Shakthi, I know how much you want Open Source to spread into the
schools and colleges of Tamil Nadu. You have more experience dealing
with students than many of us.

In our company, I work with CS graduates from small towns, whose
biggest barrier to becoming a good software engineer is language. They
are no less in problem solving or analytical skills, but English
comprehension is a barrier. Should we not give students like that the
exposure?

My point is, since the focus is on local participation, let us have
Tamil banners, promotion material also. Come to think of it, with
volunteers for other languages joining in, we can have banners etc in
Telugu, Malayalam and Hindi also. Number of Telegu speaking students
is significant in Chennai.

4. Amachu, in my opinion having a Tamil sub-conference will be
counter-productive. Communicate the message to the students in Tamil
and have them take part in the main conference.

anbudan,

Ma Sivakumar

thanks - this is the most urgent task now, especially call for  
participation
>
> 3. Shakthi, I know how much you want Open Source to spread into the
> schools and colleges of Tamil Nadu. You have more experience dealing
> with students than many of us.
>
> In our company, I work with CS graduates from small towns, whose
> biggest barrier to becoming a good software engineer is language. They
> are no less in problem solving or analytical skills, but English
> comprehension is a barrier. Should we not give students like that the
> exposure?

it is unfortunately true that english fluency is a must for a foss  
programmer. Windows people can get away without english fluency - at  
the cost of writing crap. I dont like this, the French dont like it,  
but it is inevitable. We can use local languages for publicity, but  
in the last analysis, unless a person masters English, he will not  
excel as a programmer. The problem is that when people master  
English, they forget their local language and become strangers in  
their own country.
>
> My point is, since the focus is on local participation, let us have
> Tamil banners, promotion material also. Come to think of it, with
> volunteers for other languages joining in, we can have banners etc in
> Telugu, Malayalam and Hindi also. Number of Telegu speaking students
> is significant in Chennai.

certainly
>
> 4. Amachu, in my opinion having a Tamil sub-conference will be
> counter-productive. Communicate the message to the students in Tamil
> and have them take part in the main conference.

I agree here. A tamil subconference can talk about foss, can  
contribute documentation and translation - but cannot contribute  
code. And if our conference does not produce code, and coders, it  
will be a failure.

Brief glimpse of the mail in tamil.

We gad a small discussion. Elango of MIT, myself and Shankar. 

Two things came out.

as an advocacy and awareness,

1) Calling for essays from schools and colleges from students on what is FOSS 
and its related topics.

The topics can be dynamic. Like for a Law College Students it can be

"The perils of Software Patents"

and for schools it can be

"Why we need free software for schools"

Elango can step into this job with few other students.

2) IT industry how to approach and harness its resources atleast few. if 
interested some small team can be formed with shankar for this.

Feedbacks?

Girish Venkatachalam wrote:
> Can I have a look at the slides please?

The slides can be found at http://www.bravegnu.org/#qemu

The talk covers the following:
   1. Qemu usage basics - networking, disk images
   2. writing simulations for simple parallel port peripherals
   3. writing Linux drivers for these peripherals

Hi All,

On Nov 17, 2007 1:00 PM, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
> the problem is many more people are worried about the closeness of
> the logo to various party symbols and are nervous about the effect on
> the conference and attendance. Logo is not all that important, so it
> would be better to have something totally free of controversy. This
> is especially true for the interior parts of TN where we want to do
> the most publicity.

Firstly I must frankly state is that "things are being taken a bit too far".
Niyam's logo is brilliant IMO. If someone is foolish enough to
consider a hand (it is not even actually representing the party symbol
by no means as it varies by way too much) it to be some party stuff
and hence not attend, I would be happy about him not attending.
May be you can use the new logoin banners and stuff if
The statement "Logo is not that important" is another "stupid"
statement. The logo actually goes all along the way in the coming
years if at all this is planned to be a annual event and that becomes
some kind of a Brand for the conf.

I am afraid there is more politics here being created, assumed,
discussed and wasted time upon than what actually might be there.
Another question is Are you looking at only attendance? Then you can
very well go to the beach (Marina) or even better (Besant NagAnd
another view is that the current Logo is no way close to the quality
and meaning of Niyam's logo. May be I am wrong and thats just my POV.
Can someone illustrate what the logo actually means? the stamp, the
seal etc?
ar beach, you get good crowd there too ;-)) and start speaking. You
get loads of attendance!

Looks like the organisers must re think their goals and motives or
make the statement clear as to what exactly they are looking at.

Again I say, Niyam's logo is too good to be trashed!

Reggies.

Aanjhan

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Sat Nov 17 23:10:05 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Nov 17 23:10:18 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Embedded/VLSI FOSS workshop, BMSCE, Bengalooru, Karnataka
Message-ID: <d16b1c80711170940t3a538d45l8963f3ef581933a4@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

A one-day embedded/VLSI Free/Open Source workshop at BMS College of
Engineering, Bengalooru (Bangalore), Karnataka was organized today,
Saturday, November 17, 2007.

I handled embedded, system architecture concepts, Linux device
drivers, OpenMoko introduction topics. Aanjhan addressed FOSS EDA
tools, verilog, embedded GNU/Linux labs HOWTO et. al.

http://www.bmsce.ac.in/

I would like to thank Shashank Bharadwaj for working with me during
the past few weeks in coordinating/organizing the event.

* Students were mostly from EEE/ECE background.

According to the few interested students:

* The institution management are quite willing to help/invest for the
students, but, very few takers for it.

* There are few permanent faculty, who rotate the courses that they
teach every semester. But, most of them move/prefer the Industry.

* Neither faculty nor students are very serious about exams. Day
before the exams, frequently asked questions (not FAQs!) are given to
students, and they are given freedom to write answers to questions of
their choice.

* Lab exercises are very primitive.

* In some colleges, professors collect e-mails of all students, and
send previous project code to them, asking them to change author name,
re-compile code, and submit them! Neither faculty nor students are
very concerned.

During the workshop, I did emphasize on the need to use FOSS tools to
enhance their skills, and get exposure to the Industry, FOSS
community, and the real world.

* fci wikia on BMSCE:
http://fci.wikia.com/wiki/Bangalore/BMSCE

Presentations done:

Communication Guidelines:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/communication-guidelines.pdf

i-want-2-do-project-tell-me-wat-2-do:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/i-want-2-do-project-tell-me-wat-2-do.pdf

Mailing list guidelines:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/mailing-list-etiquette.pdf

OpenMoko introduction:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/openmoko.pdf

vhdl, Linux device driver code examples available at:
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads.html

Regards,

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

On 18-Nov-07, at 12:06 AM, Sankarshan Mukhopadhyay wrote:

>> http://blog.selvaraj.us/archives/253
>
> Is an English version of the above entry available ? Since you mention
> broken implementation of Tamil in Unicode, it appears to be an
> interesting read

his thesis is that there are 247 letters in the Tamil alphabet. 12  
vowels, 18 consonants and the rest combination of vowels and  
consonants - this is a little less than other indic languages as the  
others have more consonants. He feels that one uniocde number be  
allotted to each of these 247 letters. That is separate numbers for  
ka kA ki kI ku kU  etc. Currently only 20 numbers are allotted and  
the rest are a combination of these. He further states that this  
'mistake' is due to clubbing of Tamil with other indic languages. How  
exactly Tamil is different is not elaborated.

On Nov 18, 2007 7:51 AM, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>
> do you also want a Tamil keyboard with 247 keys?

Kenneth,

Keyboard layout is different from Character encoding. Tamil keyboard
layout will remain the same. But internally each of the 247 tamil
letters will have separate slots so that sorting, character count etc
need not be a hack (as being the requirement now).

In tamil there are only 12 vowels and 18 consonants. The corresponding
numbers for Hindi is 14 and 68 (correct the no.s). Total combination
characters for Hindi would be somewhere around 1000 compared to 247
for Tamil.

anbudan,

Ma Sivakumar

On 18-Nov-07, at 8:21 AM, ????????? ?? wrote:

> Keyboard layout is different from Character encoding. Tamil keyboard
> layout will remain the same. But internally each of the 247 tamil
> letters will have separate slots so that sorting, character count etc
> need not be a hack (as being the requirement now).

sorting in Tamil is b0rked because the wrong order has been given for  
some letters in the unicode scheme. Character count is correct,  
because the current unicode scheme allots more than one character for  
all the consonant-vowel combinations.

>
> In tamil there are only 12 vowels and 18 consonants. The corresponding
> numbers for Hindi is 14 and 68 (correct the no.s). Total combination
> characters for Hindi would be somewhere around 1000 compared to 247
> for Tamil.

in kannada, telugu, not only do they combine vowel+consonant, but  
also consonant+consonant. So according to the proposed scheme the  
kannada word kshathriya would be only 2 characters long - ksha and  
thriya.

Since all Indian languages face the same problem (I dont know about  
urdu and kashmiri), there is a need for a common solution.

From rhariram at gmail.com  Sun Nov 18 17:07:41 2007
From: rhariram at gmail.com (R Hariram Aatreya)
Date: Sun Nov 18 17:07:51 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Tamil script vs other Indian scripts
Message-ID: <ad2a4f6d0711180337k3b7569d3m983c37cd32fdd77d@mail.gmail.com>

Illustration of
One difference between Tamil script & other major indian scripts
and its implications for encoding.

. No conjuncts in Tamil
  conjunct
    = samyukta akshara (in hindi/sanskrit/many other indian languages)
    = 2 consonants (shapes) coming together to form a different 3rd shape

Example 1: consider
ng + ka -> _ngka_ =
?? + ? -> _???_ (devanaagarii) =
?? + ? -> _???_ (tamil).
In devanaagarii, 2 shapes ( ??  followed by ?) goes to form ???  (a
different shape not found in the set of base vowels & consonants).
However in Tamil, the corresponding 2 shapes (?? followed by ?) still gives ???
(no change in shapes).

Example 2: consider
t + ra -> _tra_ =
?? + ? -> _???_ (devanaagarii) =
?? + ? -> _???_ (tamil)
(again a shape change in devanaagarii and none in tamil)

. So rough estimate of unique shapes in
  - Devanaagarii :
       vowels+anusvaara+visarga(15)*consonants(33)+
       consonants(33)*consonants(33)
    = 1584[+]
  - Tamil : vowels(12) * consonants(18)
    = 216

. So implication for encoding:
  considerably lesser space (factor of 7)
  to encode ALL shapes of Tamil than Devanaagarii.

[+] Assuming only 2 consonant conjuncts and all combinations being valid
(in practice there are can be 3 and 4 consonant conjuncts and
 not all combinations of consonants are valid)


hari.

From mohan.tux at gmail.com  Mon Nov 19 06:28:15 2007
From: mohan.tux at gmail.com (Mohan Sundaram)
Date: Mon Nov 19 06:28:31 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu 7.10 : logs out of X automatically
In-Reply-To: <698980.7341.qm@web8914.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <698980.7341.qm@web8914.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4740DFA7.5090302@gmail.com>

Satheesh Kumar wrote:
> 
> How to disable the touchpad? 
> 
>  Also, i think some extra packages are required in ubuntu 7.10, for
> the touch pad to work properly.
> 
> 
> what type of packages? I have installed everything shown by update manager. Found that I didn face this problem until i run on AC Power. Once i switch to battery mode i am facing  this problem. Is there any other work around?
> 
Assuming Synaptics Touchpad

Look up xorg.conf file >> Input Device Section for Synaptics.

Section "InputDevice"
         Identifier      "Synaptics Touchpad"
         Driver          "synaptics"
         Option          "SendCoreEvents"        "true"
         Option          "Device"                "/dev/psaux"
         Option          "Protocol"              "auto-dev"
         Option          "HorizScrollDelta"      "1"
         Option          "SHMConfig"
EndSection

Normally, the SHMConfig line would be missing, Introduce it and restart 
X11. Using the Synaptic frontend, install gsynaptics or qsynaptics pkg 
for a graphical frontend to configure the pad/buttons.

To just turn off the pad, give synclient off at bash prompt.

Works on my Dell with Gutsy.

Mohan

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Mon Nov 19 06:40:21 2007

Date: Mon Nov 19 06:39:55 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Tamil script vs other Indian scripts
In-Reply-To: <ad2a4f6d0711180337k3b7569d3m983c37cd32fdd77d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <ad2a4f6d0711180337k3b7569d3m983c37cd32fdd77d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <447F854E-E198-4204-949D-893DBE2E1CCC@thenilgiris.com>


On 18-Nov-07, at 5:07 PM, R Hariram Aatreya wrote:

> One difference between Tamil script & other major indian scripts
> and its implications for encoding.
>
> . No conjuncts in Tamil
>   conjunct
>     = samyukta akshara (in hindi/sanskrit/many other indian languages)
>     = 2 consonants (shapes) coming together to form a different 3rd  
> shape

there are three cases:

1. consonant + vowel becomes a new shape - tamil, kannada, telugu and  
malayalam
2. consonant + consonant becomes new shape - kannada, telugu,  
malayalam and devnagiri

which means that kannada, telugu and malayalam have even more shapes  
than devnagiri

-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/

Most of the time magazine sites have their websites in proprietary encodings
and they provide dynamic fonts in their websites. Dynamic font technology
works only Internet explorer, so you wont find any problem in viewing those
sites in internet explorer.
But if you try copy paste the contents from the above website into notepad,
you will find they are shown as junk data.

For firefox (in any platform), we have a better work around for viewing
these sites. Thats by using Padma firefox extension.
https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/873

Padma firefox extension, converts the proprietory text into unicode text on
the fly and you will be able to view the sites in unicode. You can even save
the content as unicode text.

Regards
Mugunth

On Nov 19, 2007 6:33 AM, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>
> no - afaik ordering is correct in Kannada and devnagiri. There was a
> goof up only in Tamil as the governement representative to the
> relevant conference had not done his homework. This is subject to
> correction.

That, or one representative decided that all Indian languages are same
and can have the same ordering. The latter is more likely.

The Tamil unicode encoding table is a pain to see. Anyone with
elementary knowledge of Tamil will reject it outright.

http://unicode.org/charts/PDF/U0B80.pdf

1. See the blanks after ? ? ? ? ?. For other Indian languages 3 more
slots were allocated, so tamil gets the blanks.

2. ? comes after  ? before ?. as in Hindi. In tamil ? is the last letter.

An expert can go on with more points.

There are 57 blanks in the range. One can only wonder at the wisdom of
great unifers :-(

DIT is a member of the Unicode Consortium. NRC-FOSS comes under DIT.  
NRC-FOSS has some influence with DIT. Anything presented to DIT  
through NRC-FOSS will be listened to, if not acted upon. I suggest  
proposals be formulated and presented. I had suggested that to  
Ramanraj also, but he didnt pursue it with us. This could be a useful  
subject for a sprint for fossconf also - getting large number of  
opinions on the defects in the present Tamil Unicode and suggestions  
for change. But it needs to be taken seriously and studied seriously  
and serious people be involved so a serious proposal be made rather  
than making half-baked uninformed comments. (This last sentence is  
not aimed at anyone in particular so please dont start a flame war on  
that). Anyone interested? It means contacting all the stakeholders in  
this domain and eliciting reactions/participation from them. Also  
contacting people in Sri Lanka, Malaysia and Singapur.

possible would mean that folks who look into the arcane ends of things
like rendering engines, fonts, keyboard layouts can also track and
provide assessment of changes which would (and ideally should) lead
towards a solution that is pragmatic and practical.

I'd suggest that if the defects are listed, then the fossconf can become
a venue for assessment and way forward discussions.

On Nov 20, 2007 6:37 PM, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
> Yes. Initially for allocating the space in the Unicode table, Indian
> Govt gave the ISCII as standard covers all the Indian languages, that
> is actual problem.
>
> Now join effect from our govt + other country is needed to get proper
> code space for Tamil.
>
> AFAIK in TN, there is NO unity between the people, who are responsible
> for taking this steps. Everyone wants to push his/her own idea.

I spoke to Mr. Senthilnathan, who was involved in discussions of a
committee formed to put forward proposals for correcting Tamil
Unicode. He essentially said what Bharathi says.

Every one wants to push their ideas.
Members are book publishers, tamil font developers etc.
Almost no one had proper technical understanding.

According to Mr. Senthilnathan, the case should be presented by
technical people. What are the problems of the current code space in
technical implementation? What are the solutions in line with the
policies of Unicode consortium.

He mentioned 2 points:
1. Ordering/sorting is not the goal of Unicode, it should be handled
by individual applications.
2. Character counts (2 slots for the same character) is not an Unicode
issue, but should be handled by each application.

Hariram might be able to throw more light on these points,

anbudan,

Ma Sivakumar

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Nov 22 09:54:48 2007

Date: Thu Nov 22 09:39:25 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] LJ Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0711220947001.3145-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

> Magnatune an Open Choice, iTunes and Expensive Choice by James Lees
http://www.linuxjournal.com/article/9722 James explores the DRM-free
music site Magnatunes, the company whose cheeky motto is "We are not
evil."

> LJ TIP: Redux of "Automatically Send Your rm Files to the Trash"
Last week we offered you a tip on aliasing the rm command, so that the
deleted files end up in the Trash rather than into the ether. Paul
from Switzerland and our in-house guru, Mitch Frazier, suggested some
changes as follows. First, here's what Paul said:

I don't like, I even hate, replacing dangerous commands as rm with a
seemingly safer version. There are two main reasons:

1. rm may be used by many scripts, system or personal, where the safer
command is not wanted (e.g. could overflow .Trash etc.)

2. Much more importantly, if you get used to a safe rm, you start to
use it (more) blindly, and when you are on an other machine without
safety belt you may make really bad mistakes. I have seen too many
accidents with similar redefinitions of rm with users moving to other
machines, helping colleagues, and destroying important files.

A better solution: name your safe version slightly differently. Why 
not:

alias rmt='mv --target-directory ~/.Trash'

Which reminds you that it is "rm into Trash". rmt is safe everywhere,
and not much more difficult to use than just rm. And the original rm
is still available, unchanged, for all existing scripts. Of course, it
is probably good to use rm or /bin/rm in scripts to have the original
one.

And here is Mitch Frazier's response:

I would agree with [Paul's] first point, it's probably not a good idea
to alias commands like rm in scripts. Particularly when the alias is
in another script altogether. Besides the problems he points out, you
don't want to do it because now your script won't work for anybody
else (since the alias is not in the script itself, it's in .bashrc).

The problem with the original tip is that (probably) rather than 
saying:

Put following into ~/.bashrc

it could have been:

Put following into ~/.aliases

When you put an alias in .aliases rather than in .bashrc it does not
get expanded when you run a shell script. Aliases from .aliases are
only expanded for interactive shells, ie you typing at the shell
prompt.  Putting it in .aliases, I would say, is a reasonable use of
an alias.  Personally, I'd rather make my life easier/safer during the
99.99% of the time that I'm typing on my system than worry about the
0.01% of the time when I'm working on somebody else's system. Stuff
happens everyday of the week, not just when you're at somebody else's
house.


> The Other Desktop: Running XFCE
One of Linux's greatest strengths is that it's easily customized.  
Although most distributions ship with a variety of standard tools for
specific purposes (such as sendmail as a mail server or Vixie Cron to
handle repeated jobs), alternative tools are readily available. You
can rip out just about any component, either removing it entirely or
replacing it with something else. Linux lets you remove or replace
more components than most operating systems, allowing the savvy
administrator to customize a Linux installation for specific purposes.

http://responses.linux-mag.com/ct.html?rtr=on&s=ax0v,6v82,33o,b5so,1zna,96lb,6o2h 

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

From mksarav at gmail.com  Thu Nov 22 13:01:12 2007
From: mksarav at gmail.com (M K Saravanan)
Date: Thu Nov 22 13:01:23 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Viewing tamil news sites in Firefox
In-Reply-To: <918603.35792.qm@web54507.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

On Nov 22, 2007 2:36 PM, Dhanagopal Rengasamy <dhanagopal@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Should I install indic language support for Windows XP
> to read the above
> tamil new sites in Firefox?  It requires 250 mb of
> space.

To view Indian Language Unicode characters properly, enabling Indic
lang support is a must in Windows XP and it has nothing to do with the
particular browser.



> Both in Ubuntu 7.10 and Windows XP, I have installed
> the firefox extension
> Padma 0.4.11  to read the tamil news sites.
> The problem is soon after opening the sites in
> firefox, the fonts areI
> displayed properly only for a few a seconds. Then it
> reverted to junk
> characters.
> What should I do for proper display of tamil fonts?

I have never used any extension to see the news sites mentioned in the
original post.  I just installed the respective fonts of the news
website (for the first 3) and for thatstamil you need to enable Indic
lang support since it is already using Unicode/UTF-8.

For proprietary encoded fonts, some time changing your font encoding
to "ISO-8859-1" will help (for e.g. vikatan will show junk characters
in Firefox even if you have installed vikatan fonts given in their
website, but if you change the character encoding to iso-8859-1, then
you can read them properly :-)  That's what I am doing for the last
few years.

On Nov 22, 2007 7:38 AM, Suresh Ramasubramanian <linux@frodo.hserus.net> wrote:
> Arun Mehta (moderator of the india-gii list) is based out of Delhi and his

As mentioned by Suresh above Arun Mehta is indeed the person to
contact w.r.t to this subject. I've been in touch with him through
email, discussing the software he wrote that I just mentioned.

> They are the best people for this .. in fact they have developed some
> software for Stephen Hawking to replace his existing system.
>

The name of the software that they developed is eLocutor. The relevant
urls about this software are the following:
http://www.radiophony.com/html_files/download3.html
http://sourceforge.net/projects/hawking
http://groups.yahoo.com/group/radiophony/

The third url is for a discussion group about eLocutor among other
things. It requires one to be a member of the group to view messages,
so unfortunately discussions cannot be followed from the outside.

Like I said above, I'm pretty familiar with this program and can walk
people through how it works, if Arun Mehta is not available for some
reason.

eLocutor is Free Software, under the GPL (v2). The urls I have just
mentioned provide a thorough explanation of  what the constraints were
that led to it being designed the way it was.

The two sentence version is that it assumes the user of the program is
capable of just two voluntary motions, to press and release a button,
or press, hold for a while and then release. With those two voluntary
actions a user can create text, edit it, save it, etc and/or have the
program speak out what they have typed.

The program is written in VB, and is therefore currently Windows only.
As I recall, I had discussed with you what programming language to use
to port it to Linux.

Unfortunately, I haven't been able to follow up on those discussions
and ideas. I'm still intend to do it if no one else does it first.

I can put you in touch with additional people who can give a
perspective of a would-be user and /or parents and teachers working
with people with cerebral palsy.

I'm out of Chennai right now, but when I return you are most welcome
to come and get a first hand look at the challenges involved in
computing for people with cerebral palsy, and also at various pieces
of hardware and software that are being used, including some pretty
cool stuff that got developed very recently.

I'll be back in a few days. Anytime from the 29th November onwards is ok for me.

time
         stock tickers. The UI is not great but far better than the previous
one.
     b) Advanced - Offers real time data. It requires a java enabled
browser(IE/Firefox)
          But also says the desired OS is windows. - I havent tried this so
I am just not sure
          about its compatiblity with a java enabled firefox on linux.
3) Icicidirect.com- On date this is the best interface I have seen. Works
without any issues
     on firefox. It doesnt offer real time stock tickers. Leaving alone the
brokerage concerns
     I would say this is by far the best on terms of features and usability.

interface(probably with AJAX) so
thats its totally comaptible with firefox on linux.

On Friday 23 Nov 2007, Harish S wrote:
>
> >From my experience I have seen that any trading website which claim
> > to offer
>
> real time data
> of stock quotes(stock tickers) require Microsoft VM and IE.

> 1) Bonanzaonline.com is one such website which has a horrible
> interface and also
>     requires Microsoft VM and IE

Such incompatibility issues have been raised time and again.  It not 
just trading sites but newspapers (asian age), e-Governance sites that 
require IE because the server sends VBscript to the browser!  

It boils down to following of standards.  But then many believe that IE 
is the defacto standard and not W3C.   Most of the sites are developed 
on a tender basis where the client (here the trading company) probably 
does not specify compatability with W3C, so the contracting company 
takes the easy way out (or perhaps the team only knows IIS and IE 
platform).  Suggest you write directly to the head honcho of the 
company with a couple of screen shots of the site and see if you can 
elicit any response.  If not, you may have to keep looking.  
Unfortunately, many such companies truly believe that IE is the only 
browser out there.  Sigh :(

-- Arun Khan

Hi,

--- Baskar wrote:
| Looking for everyone's feedback and suggestions
\--

Some feedback:

1. Why FOSS for education?

The first reason should be 'freedom'. Cost is secondary. The first
reason always registers in peoples' mind, strongly, compared to the
other points. So, it is important.

2. The Most Popular FOSS Programs

Linux is a kernel, not an OS.

3. The Most Popular FOSS Programs

Statements with "#1" are quite debatable. You need to give some
statistics, or just mention as popular. That is good enough.

4. Put a license in the documentation that mentions how this
documentation can be distributed/re-used.

5. Avoid giving private/college data in your screenshots. Use dummy data.

It is ok to mention it, but, don't give their internal contact details
(unless you have permission from them).

6. For some pictures that you have used or copied from some website
(like Linus Torvalds, RMS), give source web link as to from where you
have taken it from.

The desktop screenshots are yours, so they are ok.

Overall, you have provided good coverage of available applications.

On a side note, your screenshots show that you have logged to X as
root user. Do you use your desktop like that?

Regards,

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From indianathann at gmail.com  Sat Nov 24 10:56:42 2007
From: indianathann at gmail.com (Padhu Indianathann)
Date: Sat Nov 24 10:56:53 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux on Pendrive - Reg
Message-ID: <e43212340711232126va86016ao9bea4e5f16e92fe2@mail.gmail.com>

Dear LUGs,
                I tried 1GB Scandisk cruzer pen Drive for Linux booting drive.
I tried various distros,

1. Puppy Linux 3.0
        It is easy to use. Puppy universal Installer makes easy to
configure USB as boot drive. Tinny space occupation (90MB). It can
make USB as bootable without MBR. It will work on all SATA, PATA HHD
contained PCs. It is required minimum 256 MB USB.

2. Slax (200 MB)
        It is an wonderful and small Linux for USB. But creation of
USB work on the same pc or same type of PCs. If creation PC contains
single HHD, then you use in PC having 2 HHD booting problem caused. It
is required minimum 256 MB USB. feather Linux and RUNT website are not
available but many websites shows its installation guidelines.

3. Pendrive Linux (400MB)
        It is an excellent debian flavour linux and easy to create USB
drive on both Linux and Windows. But same problem as in slax using.It
is required 512 MB USB but 1GB is better.

4. Ubuntu Linux
       It is an standard CD.ISO image used to create USB boot drive.
But it required minimum 1GB USB pendrive but 2GB is best.

          Just i tried. If any other distros tried by anybody please
post your experience.

I also required an a guide to manual pendrive Linux creation tutorial
from ISO files. or any other tutorial to create LInux OS boot device
by using kernel, individual packages.

N.Padmanathan.

From vijaykumar at bravegnu.org  Sat Nov 24 17:58:18 2007
From: vijaykumar at bravegnu.org (Vijay Kumar)
Date: Sat Nov 24 17:58:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Strangeness in qemu routing table
In-Reply-To: <20071124115938.GA31622@saraswathy.susmita.org>
References: <20071124115938.GA31622@saraswathy.susmita.org>
Message-ID: <474818E2.7070406@bravegnu.org>

Girish Venkatachalam wrote:
> Hello friends,
> 
> Can someone please educate me on how qemu networking works?
> 
> I believe it is some kind of special bridging but I am really confused
> how packets travel back and forth with the 'weird' routing table I see.

Are you using usermode networking? (Qemu has two networking modes tap 
and usermode)

In usermode networking, for every TCP/UDP socket opened within the 
guest, qemu opens a corresponding TCP/UDP socket in the host. Qemu does 
this by snooping the ethernet frames that it receives from the network 
cards emulated by qemu. This block diagram shows the various stacks 
involved and their role in user mode networking -- 
http://www.bravegnu.org/qemu/qemu-usernet.png

Regards,
Vijay

be like Canaonical people (well, foss is good and everything but we

Microsoft? (well atleast Microsoft does not claim they are a foss
company). I think it is on topic because similar actions by other
members of the community didn't go well with the community.

Then there is also the Firefox logo trademark issue and iceweasel.
Lets not repeat the mistakes.

> Are you using usermode networking? (Qemu has two networking modes tap 
> and usermode)
> 

Yes. Apparently.

> In usermode networking, for every TCP/UDP socket opened within the 
> guest, qemu opens a corresponding TCP/UDP socket in the host. Qemu does 
> this by snooping the ethernet frames that it receives from the network 
> cards emulated by qemu. This block diagram shows the various stacks 
> involved and their role in user mode networking -- 

Great. That explains why GRE and ICMP packets don't go thro'.

Many thanks.

Girish

http://www.debian.org/logos/    <----- there are two types of license  
for logos here. I like the official use logo license, but it can be  
discussed. The license should, in my opinion, be like this:

0. This logo has been designed by Niyam Bhushan and the copyright for  
it has been assigned to FossConf
1. The copyright of this logo belongs to FossConf
2. This logo, or a modification of it may be only used to refer to  
the FossConf.
3. If this logo, or a modification of it is used on a web page, a  
link to the FossConf website - currently http:// 
registration.fossconf.in/web/ *must* be added.
4. The use of this logo by any product, organisation or site does not  
indicate that the said product, organisation or site is endorsed by  
FossConf.
5. Since FossConf is not yet a legal entity, the copyright of the  
logo is being held by NRC-FOSS on behalf of FossConf until such time  
as FossConf becomes a legal entity.

6. [optional] This logo may be used to sell toothpaste provided the  
said toothpaste is free and does not contain any proprietary  
ingredients or formulae. However this does not imply that the said  
toothpaste is endorsed by FossConf.

On 24-Nov-07, at 2:47 PM, balachandar muruganantham wrote:

> adding this list,
> this line from the bottom "copyright 2007
> NRC-FOSS<webmaster@nrcfosshelpline.in>" should be removed. again do we
> support copyright / copyleft?

the conference software is copyrighted by NRC-FOSS. It is free  
software released under the BSD license. The source code and license  
are available at https://svn.nrcfosshelpline.in/public/conference.  
The same are also viewable on the conference trac wiki http:// 
registration.fossconf.in/code/. The person who writes the software  
gets the copyright and gets to decide what license to use. I wrote/am  
writing the software and I have decided to use the BSD license. I  
have assigned the license to NRC-FOSS which is releasing it under the  
BSD license. As for the contents of the website, I agree that it  
should be under some creative commons license - I will modify the  
footer to reflect the same. This is a generic footer that we put on  
all our sites - thanks for pointing out the difference between the  
conference software and the content.

From mbchandar at gmail.com  Sun Nov 25 14:10:58 2007
From: mbchandar at gmail.com (balachandar muruganantham)
Date: Sun Nov 25 14:11:15 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Few suggestions on Registration Process on fossconf website
Message-ID: <dc538c3f0711250040i5f9503fcm73a82f418da95afc@mail.gmail.com>

Current Steps for Registration

1. Login here http://registration.fossconf.in/web/register/ and  give
username and email address
2. You will get a key in your email
3. clicking on it takes you to
http://registration.fossconf.in/web/adduser/[some<http://registration.fossconf.in/web/adduser/%5Bsome>autogenerated
number]/ where it asks again for username and password. on
giving username, password and confirm password, it goes to login page
without saying anything

What needs to be changed here
1. Step 1 is good and let autogenerate password here and send to specified
email here instead of making 3 steps registration process. lets give the
user the flexibility of changing the password at first login.
2.http://registration.fossconf.in/web/addtalk/ and
http://registration.fossconf.in/web/managetalks/
should be visible only after user login. say user home page.

Bug kind of....
1. After receiving key from the registration email, if i once registered,
key should not be active again. but at present it still active. i go there
to re-register and if i give username and password (both same) , it shows me
the exceptions (IntegrityError...). we  need to avoid this.

Usability issues
1. After receiving key from the registration email, i go there to register
my username(re-entering). it would be good if it automaticaly shows the
username rather than re-entering

Logo / Name correction
i see the text "FossConf". i guess it should be FOSSConf rather than
FossConf as FOSS is abbreviated to Free and Open Source Software (correct me
if i am wrong). what Foss mean here? can someone please explain.

From: linuxlingam at gmail.com (Linux Lingam)
Date: Mon Nov 26 03:51:17 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Why FOSS for Education, a presentation in PDF format
Message-ID: <68ddcb070711251421u3403d347n1a7e2d8a96d24449@mail.gmail.com>

dear all,

a few days ago baskar sent the following email and link to a presenation on
the list:

Date: Fri, 23 Nov 2007 18:06:58 +0530 (IST)
From: "Baskar Selvaraj" <baskar@linuxpertsystem.com>
Subject: [Ilugc] Why FOSS for Education, a presentation in PDF format
To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
Message-ID: <20071123123714.3C4E01DB25A@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"

  Hi all,

  Looking for everyone's feedback and suggestions

  http://linuxbaskar.googlepages.com/free-software-for-education.pdf

  Baskar
  LinuXpert Systems


just read through the excellent presentation. a few suggestions:

a) please publish this under an FDL or similar copyleft license, on a public
repository with sourcefiles, so others may contribute and enrich this
further.

b) please add video-edit software such as kino. camcoders are becoming
digital commodities.

c) show openclipart.org, as well as galleries of openoffice.org templates
from the web.

d) show migration from windows, how contacts, emails, bookmarks, and other
data flies in.

e) google-earth on the desktop. i now this is not a foss software, so
perhaps you could show maps in the browser.

f) a digital photo of a computer booting with gnulinux on a thumbdrive.

g) shots of foss events in india: this to show the vibrant and growing
community around foss.

h) since this is targeted to academia, hence a bit more on learning
management systems, moodle, schoolforge, etc. this usually works as a pretty
solid clincher in academia, from my experience.

i) finally, my favourite screenshot: solitaire. this gets a few chuckles and
laughs, but everyone tends to identify with this, and this eases everyone's
attitude towards gnulinux as a desktop: yes! it can be used for frivolous
and fun stuff as well.

j) i would change the amarok screenshot to show the genres of net
radio-stations by genre.


:-)
-- 
niyam bhushan

From vaidhy at gmail.com  Mon Nov 26 10:16:08 2007
From: vaidhy at gmail.com (Vaidhyanathan Mayilrangam Gopalan)

ILUGC is not the entity here.. Members of ILUGC are organizing it.. But 
ILUGC is a superset.

Further, like all other previous discussions (flamewars) we had, ILUGC 
is about discussing Linux primarily and FOSS to some extent.

Also, carrying to the logical conclusion, if Deepan and I decide to do 
a cricket tournament (for ILUGs) and start using ILUGC to discuss stuff, 
all of you would be pointing out that ILUGC is not the right place and 
you do not need to know what our logo is or how many balls we got. We 
would reply saying that Deepan and I are members of ILUGC, so ILUGC is 
organizing the tournament and hence we should discuss anything we want 
on the mailing list. Next time, it will be a discussion on political 
activity, language  stuff and soon a free for all.

By the same logic, I am not organizing Fossconf and I do not want to 
know the details. I am member of ILUGC because I use Linux and am 
interested in its development.

Why should I get spammed with the details of Fossconf when it is not the 
primary purpose of the mailing list? There is also something known as 
"tyranny of the majority..." at which point this argument also 
degenerates into another flamewar :)

Cheers,
Vaidhy

Vaidhyanathan Mayilrangam Gopalan wrote:
> ILUGC is not the entity here.. Members of ILUGC are organizing it..
>  But ILUGC is a superset.

Its not just the memebrs, the LUG itself is an organizer with NRCFOSS.

> Also, carrying to the logical conclusion, if Deepan and I decide to
>  do a cricket tournament (for ILUGs) and start using ILUGC to
> discuss stuff, all of you would be pointing out that ILUGC is not
> the right place and you do not need to know what our logo is or how
> many balls we got.
Does Crikcet and FOSSConf fall into the same category? Explained
below, why FOSSConf is more important to this mailing list.
>
> By the same logic, I am not organizing Fossconf and I do not want
> to know the details. I am member of ILUGC because I use Linux and
> am interested in its development.
Then just discard the mails falling into this topic, set a filter to
do so. May be we can add a [FOSSConf] tag to all future mailing list
to help people set their filters appropriately?

>
> Why should I get spammed with the details of Fossconf when it is
> not the primary purpose of the mailing list?

[1] The primary purpose of a LUG is to spread the awareness about
GNU/Linux and also FOSS. We haven't been speaking just about GNU/Linux
here, but a lot of things related to FOSS as well.

[2] FOSSConf is one another endeavor of ILUGC with NRCFOSS, and it
pertains to FOSS and GNU/Linux. Hence it is not an OT to this list and
as ILUGC is organizing this, it is wise to be discussed in in ILUGC"s
public mailing list so that everyone interested can participate in
this. Discussions also get into the archives which serves as a future
reference.

If we start creating mailing list for each and every
conference|workshop that we organize, for just a mere fact that a few
in the mailing list do not care about it, then we are going to end up
with a dozen such lists, while on the other hand the main list will be
totally blank about whats happening.

On Mon, 26 Nov 2007 06:56:12 +0530, Kenneth Gonsalves
<lawgon@thenilgiris.com> said:  

> On 25-Nov-07, at 2:40 PM, Praveen A wrote:

>>> My gut says t go with the GPL -- I mean, trust people not to use a
>>> logo which says "Fossconf chennai feb 2008" to refer to something
>>> else, really. Or allow modification, but ask for a name change
>>> (don't refer to fossconf in the derived work).

> I want to prevent people using the graphics and their own words
>>> 
>>> In lots of situations, less control works out OK.  On the other
>>> hand, if you treat people like criminals, they tend to behave like
>>> that.
>>> 
>> 
>> I would also like to see the logo under GPL.

> GPL is not meant for logos - it is for software

        Logos are software.  That is the Debian view as well -- computer
 related stuff is either hardware, software, or wetware.  Clearly, logos
 are represented on computer hard drives as zeros and ones, and are,
 tus, software.

>> 
>>> Is there any credible harm that a restrictive license is shielding
>>> us from?
>> 
>> Exactly what are we going to gain by this restriction? Preventing
>> some other foss conference using it?

> I personally dont mind if another foss conference uses it - but Niyam
> has made it so good that lots of other people would be tempted to use
> it for their products.

        Just as Debian makes software so good that other people are
 tempted to use it for their products.  Like canonical. Or Xandros.

        Having our creative products used by other people is what free
 software is all about.  Retain copyrights. Feed back improvements. Use
 our creative efforts for whatever you want, or need, to.

        I am surprised I am having to remind people about this on this
 forum.

        manoj

> GNU/Linux and also FOSS. We haven't been speaking just about GNU/Linux
> here, but a lot of things related to FOSS as well.


when i joined ILUGC, it was purely a GNU/Linux mailing list where i
discussed a lot, my issues got it resolved from people. now a days, i do not
see such technical discussions. most discussions involve broadband
connectivity(repeatably being asked), FOSS philosophy etc

i guess ILUGC being diverted from a technical mailing list to a general
mailing list (this is purely my opinion)

[2] FOSSConf is one another endeavor of ILUGC with NRCFOSS, and it
> pertains to FOSS and GNU/Linux. Hence it is not an OT to this list and
> as ILUGC is organizing this, it is wise to be discussed in in ILUGC"s
> public mailing list so that everyone interested can participate in
> this. Discussions also get into the archives which serves as a future
> reference.
>
> If we start creating mailing list for each and every
> conference|workshop that we organize, for just a mere fact that a few
> in the mailing list do not care about it, then we are going to end up
> with a dozen such lists, while on the other hand the main list will be
> totally blank about whats happening.
>
I agree. but ppl should also remember there is a non-tech ILUGC mailing list

 and creative property, then perhaps true advocated of freedom need to
 start boycotting it?

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Mon Nov 26 16:57:55 2007
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Mon Nov 26 16:58:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Fossconf -08 
Message-ID: <247460.76924.qm@web7903.mail.in.yahoo.com>

Dear All

        Regarding FOSSConf-08 several questions/doubts/objections
were raised. Let me try to answer/explain some of them.

a.Decision making. Who and how?
    This conference is jointly organised by ILUGC and NRCFOSS.
    We have formed a committee to take responsibility for 
    conducting the conference. From ILUGC side following
    are members

1. Raman P  raamanp at yahoo.co.in 
2. Bharathi  sbharathi at midascomm.com 
3. B Vijayakumar  vijaykumar at bravegnu.org 
4. A Saravanan  saran at lynusacademy.com 
5. Baskar
6. Srinivasan T 
7. Bhuvaneswaran A  bhuvan at ubuntu.com 
8. Vamsee Kanakala  vamsee at viamentis.com 
9. Joe Steeve  joe_steeve at gmx.net 
10. Senthil Kumaran S  stylesen at gmail.com 
11. Raja Subramanian  rajasuperman at gmail.com 
12. G.P.Pragadeeswaran (MIT)  computersociety.mit at gmail.com 

     The members were those who were active in organising/
participating in previous events[ some declined due to 
various reasons].

       NRCFOSS has nominated few members Dr.Srinivasan,KG,Shriramdas,
Ponnusamy.

      Most of the decisions are taken/will be taken after due
consultation with committee members.

b. New Members : We welcome new members, if they are willing to
  be 'physical volunteer'. They have to take responsibility to
  co-ordinate a task - like publicity, stall arrangement - etc.
  They must be able to spare time during the event, be present
  there, organise.
  More important take responsibility for fame/blame for the
  success/failure of the event.
  

c.We (here I mean the committee members) are NOT interested in
  'spamming' (borrowing word from vaidhy) the list. As of
  now only points raised were related to logo, website. 
  Whenever  we feel, it is better to get opinion from larger
  segment we approach the list.

d.I will be posting a summary of what is going on in the 
  committee once a week now onwards, and once in 2-3 days
  from Jan 15 2008 onwards. Hope that will not be considered
  spamming.

e.All your suggesstions can be recorded in the wiki pages
  of registration.fossconf.in.

f.You can also send me mail offlist for anything related
  to the event.


   I request all of you to take interest in making the conference a
grand success.


Raman.P

Message-ID: <3f2beab60711260716p60557e08s5ecfd1a7da16634e@mail.gmail.com>

2007/11/25, Manoj Srivastava <srivasta@debian.org>:
> On Mon, 26 Nov 2007 06:23:18 +0530, Kenneth Gonsalves
> <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> said:
>
> > On 24-Nov-07, at 9:55 PM, Praveen A wrote:
>
> >> If we don't practice what we preach, then what is the point, we would
> >> be like Canaonical people (well, foss is good and everything but we
> >> are spending money developing launchpad, no? and foss is just for
> >> stuff _you_ get it for free not what you develop). They have all the
> >> legal right to do so but then what makes them different from
> >> Microsoft? (well atleast Microsoft does not claim they are a foss
> >> company). I think it is on topic because similar actions by other
> >> members of the community didn't go well with the community.
>
> > what exactly are you trying to say here? Is it your thesis that any
> > company that promotes, develops or distributes opensource/free
> > software should not at the same time use, develop or distribute closed
> > source software?
>

I'm in the community because I like being part of it. I spent my time
here because I feel it is useful to the community. I look at other
people's commitment by looking at how much they are giving back to the
community. So whenever I see someone who does not play well with the
community (Novell with their patent trap and Canonical with their
non-free launchpad) I decide not to play with them (I hope there are
others in the community who share the same view). because there are
others in the community who needs my time whom I can count on to  be
with the community come what may happen (Debian Social contract,
Fedora's commitment to Open Source, Utoto's commitment to Free
Software...). So I spent my time (and I have all the rights to decide
that) with those who have a demonstrated commitment to the community
and who give back.

So in this case if the FOSSConf goes the non-free way I will stop
supporting it, stop promoting it... Because there are other
conferences which respects the community and who does not treat people
like criminals who would value my time spent with them.

>         I am of the school of thought that freedom helps people achive
>  their greatest potential. That hoarding knowledge hurts people, by
>  restricting their freedom. That we can stand on shoulder of giants only
>  when the giant's shoulders are not locked up, and only released for
>  pay.
>
>         If a free software conference can't stop hoarding information
>  and creative property, then perhaps true advocated of freedom need to
>  start boycotting it?
>
>         manoj

+2

I completely agree with Manoj here. I'm surprised  how everyone in the
foss community thinks it is OK to be non-free when it is "my stuff".
Especially here it was not even original contribution (like
canonical), it was contributed by the community.

Cheers
Praveen

On Mon, 26 Nov 2007 14:38:41 +0530, Kenneth Gonsalves
<lawgon@thenilgiris.com> said:  

> On 26-Nov-07, at 11:39 AM, Manoj Srivastava wrote:

>>> GPL is not meant for logos - it is for software
>> 
>> Logos are software.  That is the Debian view as well -- computer
>> related stuff is either hardware, software, or wetware.  Clearly,
>> logos are represented on computer hard drives as zeros and ones, and
>> are, tus, software.

> not so. It so happens that this logo was designed using a computer. It
> could as well have been designed using paint and paper. And it will be
> mostly distributed on paper, cloth and other materials. And
> modifications made may not be made on the computer. Next you will be
> saying that a building designed on a computer is software

        You are mixing up abstract concepts and instanciations of the
 concept. The Logo, as it stands, can have multiple representations --
 some of which are hardware (when printed on paper and ink) -- and it
 has a software representation.

        Conceptually, they are different instanciations/representations
 of the same abstract entity -- and one of these representations is
 software.


        So, a building blueprint can indeed have a software
 representation.

>> Just as Debian makes software so good that other people are tempted
>> to use it for their products.  Like canonical. Or Xandros.

> they use the debian logo?

        They use Debian intellectual property.

>> Having our creative products used by other people is what free
>> software is all about.  Retain copyrights. Feed back
>> improvements. Use our creative efforts for whatever you want, or
>> need, to.

> this doesnt apply to logos - and debian itself agrees.

        No.  The Debian official logo is non-free -- we realize that.
 It is never shipped by any Debian product, since our products are all
 fee. Check it out.

        Having a non-free official logo is a blot on our name -- which
 is why it is so rarely used. Our website uses the free logo, for
 instance.

        manoj

Shrinivasan T wrote:
> please give me your advices on giving a talk.
1. Do a demo of installing GNU/Linux as a dual boot machine. What
Raman and me did was to follow this by asking one of the students to
come forward and try installing the same over again. This gives
confidence among the students that when one of their buddies is able
to do it, then they can do it too.
2. Do not talk too much of philosophy. Students just drop them as
stories. Make them understand the importance of such philosophies by
giving practical examples. I love the way Raman gives examples for
stuff and even have them by-hearted ;)
3. As far as possible, after you show them something call 2 students
(from each gender) and ask them to try doing this themselves. This
will improve the confidence level among students and after a few
rounds they will actually compete to come and do things :)
>
> Is there any presentation available that you used for prevoius sessions,
> please share with me.
I am somehow lost the presentation which we used. You can get it from
Raman, but I will suggest making a new copy of it, updating some of
the data/statistics present in the slides. :)

On Nov 27, 2007 11:06 AM, Padhu Indianathann <indianathann@gmail.com> wrote:
> Dear LUGs,
>         Any GUI mode utility for Secure copy between LInux PCs like
> WinSCP in windows and gftp in Linux for FTP server access.
>

Nautilus does a pretty good job. You can browse the remote machine by
pressing Ctrl+L and typing ssh://<machinename>/, and cut-copy-paste to
it like a normal folder. Of course, it uses ssh as a backend, so its
pretty secure.

  I am sorry for suggesting this late, but it is worth to discuss.

Conference", whereas Australia, Taiwan, Israel, and may be some other 
countries have OSDC.  Why not we call FossConf as OSDC India ?  This 
will receive global visibility.  I'm right now in Brisbane attending

become a part of "Open Source Developers Club". More info at

conference may be very difficult at this stage. We can consider it as an

acquiring FOSS is much lower. what about TCO?
3. i disagree with second paragragh on page 6. where it says that FOSS
performs better than the proprietory softwares....
4. page 10 says rms started developing a free operation system called GNU
which is wrong. rms started a GNU project to create a unix-like operation
system. more over rms and linus did not plan and started the project. i
think its a grammer mistake
5. page 15. Linux is not the server OS. its a kernel
6. page 15. Apache is not a web server. Its a collection of projects. say it
as Apache HTTP Server Project. how do you know that it is #1 web server on
the internet?
7. page 16. MySQL's market share could never grow faster than windows.:)
please correct it. i think you want to compare with MSSQL.
8. page 62. scilab demo seems to be taken from windows vista.
9. for GIMP and Inkscape, QCAD, please change the title. for GIMP you could
say Graphical Image manipulation Program, for Inkscape, Vector Drawing
Program. in first few slides, you have said that FOSS performs better than
proprietary and here you are promoting using proprietary software names. i
agree it will catch people's mind but lets tell them what it is...
10. page 116 . Linux is included in FOSS. so change the title as "Useful
Websites on FOSS"
11. BOSS is not a popular linux i guess...check here
http://linux.about.com/od/popular_distros/Popular_Linux_Distributions.htm
12. in experts excerpt, can u please keep kalam's talk first
13. page 131 says "New technology developments using FOSS.". can you tell me
what are all new developments going on?

>

> discussion at some point.
>
>> your comments on the topic are?
>
> My personal choice is CC or GFDL.
>
> But as Conf organizer, How do you protect that the same logo is NOT
> used for a Conf/Event with same name, but expanded like "Frustrated
> Open Source Software user Conf". Do we need to worry about this?

I was doing some research and find that most people tend to license  
their logos as they license their software - with the exception of  
Mozilla and Linux foundation who are very strict. And, of course,  
Debian! Anyway our logo is composed of a Bharatanatyam mudra - which  
is thousands of years old and cannot be claimed by anyone, and a  
pottu which is worn by millions of women all over the world - again  
cannot be claimed by anyone. It is quite possible that a combination  
of the two has already been used - maybe in hundreds of ways. So lets  
license it under the BSD license - which is the freest of all  
licenses - and make everyone happy. After all, we cannot really  
justify any sort of restriction on the use, commercial or otherwise,  
of pottu and mudra.

From: baskar at linuxpertsystem.com (Baskar Selvaraj)
Date: Tue Nov 27 19:06:03 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Why FOSS for Education, a presentation in PDF format
Message-ID: <20071127133555.7C4C51DB257@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>


1. document in pdf format which is proprietory

The presentation/document will be released under FDL soon, after making necessary modifications.

2. Page 4 talks abt Lower Costs. it is mentioned that Initial Cost of
acquiring FOSS is much lower. what about TCO?
3. i disagree with second paragragh on page 6. where it says that FOSS
performs better than the proprietory softwares....
If in doubt, pl. go through the statistics given by David Wheeler at www.dwheeler.com

5. page 15. Linux is not the server OS. its a kernel.
In my programme, I clarify the students that, Linux is just a kernel and not operating system.

6. page 15. Apache is not a web server. Its a collection of projects. say it
as Apache HTTP Server Project. how do you know that it is #1 web server one
the internet?
The statistics were taken from www.dwheeler.com

7. page 16. MySQL's market share could never grow faster than windows.:)
please correct it. i think you want to compare with MSSQL.
Yes, the comparison was made with MS-SQL only.

8. page 62. scilab demo seems to be taken from windows vista.
Scilab and gCAD3d screenshots were taken from the project websites and not captured under F-7.

4. page 10 says rms started developing a free operation system called GNU
which is wrong. rms started a GNU project to create a unix-like operation
system. more over rms and linus did not plan and started the project. i
think its a grammer mistake

The above was included for an average computer student to understand that, most of the
FOSS developments were initially developed in an academic environment and nothing else.

9. for GIMP and Inkscape, QCAD, please change the title. for GIMP you could 
say Graphical Image manipulation Program, for Inkscape, Vector Drawing
Program. in first few slides, you have said that FOSS performs better than
proprietary and here you are promoting using proprietary software names. i
agree it will catch people's mind but lets tell them what it is...

The students whom I am focussing were much exposed to Proprietory software by their 
names.  So, it becomes necessary to have a comparison of name with the equivalent
proprietory softwares and I have never used/recommended the proprietory softwares I have mentioned
in the slide.  (My company's policy is strictly not to use proprietory software for any work).

11. BOSS is not a popular linux i guess...check here
http://linux.about.com/od/popular_distros/Popular_Linux_Distributions.htm

BOSS was included not because of its popularity. To make aware among the students that, India
too has its own distribution called BOSS (Bharat Operating System Solutions).


12. in experts excerpt, can u please keep kalam's talk first
ok, the students pay more attention for Kalam's talk when shown in the last, and nothing else.

13. page 131 says "New technology developments using FOSS.". can you tell me
what are all new developments going on?

1.  We have developed a new storage/backup solution completed based on free softwares.

Samba + Rsync + Heartbeat Clustering.

The above setup will ensure 99.9% of Reliable Data backup for organisations of any size (SME/Large Enterprises) when combined with Heartbeat clustering.

2. We have developed our own Terminal Server solution based on Free softwares (for Linux / Windows Servers) which we have
given freely to many Engineering / Arts and Science Colleges in Tamilnadu to setup FOSS Labs.

3. We also have a huge collection of FOSS softwares about 4000 GB, which you can browse the list at

http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/?title=CDs_for_Grab#Pazhavanthangal

Any institution in Tamilnadu can get the Free softwares from us totally free of cost.

Baskar
LinuXpert Systems

It will be more useful, if you could prepare atleast few students for long
term projects..  The students would have no idea on how to start  a
project..

SO we could do some research on how to bring interested newbies, gradually
and step by step, towards participating in any of the major open source
projects.

The base line here is that in addition to imparting knowledge, we need to
mentor few students there, who after getting enough exposure to the FOSS
projects, will in turn, train their juniors, before they leave the college.

By this, we can create replicating talent centers in more colleges, and then
later co-ordinate their activities.


Just my thoughts, which i wished to implement in the near future.

----- On 11/28/07, Bama <chorse@gmail.com> wrote:
| until I installed azerus. I'm not
| sure about the ports or the firewall it triggered,

Why would azureus alter your port settings?

-----
| apparently now I'm not
| able to use browsers, but
| from commmand line I could ping almost all sites.
\--

Which means your connection is ok, "/etc/resolv.conf" and "/sbin/route
-n" are correct. Can you post output of:

  cat /etc/resolv.conf
  /sbin/route -n

You can save outputs to a file:

  /sbin/route -n > route.txt

Can you check your browser settings?

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Nov 28 16:45:32 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Nov 28 16:30:20 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] LJ Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0711281643440.3792-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

LJ Tech Tip: Can't Get Enough of Aliases

Aliases are really handy, if you seldom use the command line and your
memory is as bad as mine. They are also an essential time saving tool if
you live on the command line. But, they clutter up your command line
history file and make it harder to use, too.

There is a bash setting that can be used to prevent this by excluding some
of the more common commands like ls, etc.... Ones that you don't really
need in the history file. If you list all of your aliases there it will
exclude them as well. If you can remember an alias' name you don't need to
look it up in the history. :-)

If you put these two entries in your ~/.bash_profile or ~/.bashrc file the
following environment variables will be available every time you start up a
shell, and really reduce history clutter.

export HISTCONTROL=erasedups
export HISTIGNORE="dir*:cd *:ls*:less *:&"

HISTCONTROL=erasedups is an option that removes all previous duplicate
lines before saving to the history list. The option "ignorespace" prevents
lines which begin with a space from being saved in the history list. This
allows you, on an individual basis, to select which commands go into the
history file by putting a space before the command.

HISTIGNORE="" takes a list of commands (including shell wildcards) that you
don't want in the historyfile. A colon is used as the separator and "&" is
a special symbol that causes history to ignore consequtive duplicate
commands.

When HISTIGNORE is used with SUSE 10.3, there has to be a space before the
"*" in the commands cd and less -- but if you used a space with dir or ls,
it did not work properly. So you will have to do a little experimenting and
testing to get it working the way you want.

To immediately reload changes in ~/.bashrc, simply type source ~/.bashrc
and press enter, in a terminal window.

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

Did you tried Damn Small Linux (DSL)?

*DSL is a very versatile 50MB mini desktop oriented Linux distribution.*

Damn Small is small enough and smart enough to do the following things:

   - Boot from a business card CD as a live linux distribution (LiveCD)
   - Boot from a USB pen drive
   - Boot from within a host operating system (that's right, it can run
   *inside* Windows)
   - Run very nicely from an IDE Compact Flash drive via a method we call
   "frugal install"
   - Transform into a Debian OS with a traditional hard drive install
   - Run light enough to power a 486DX with 16MB of Ram
   - Run fully in RAM with as little as 128MB (you will be amazed at how
   fast your computer can be!)
   - Modularly grow -- DSL is highly extendable without the need to
   customize

From knura at yahoo.com  Thu Nov 29 13:44:17 2007
From: knura at yahoo.com (Arun Khan)
Date: Thu Nov 29 13:44:36 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] urgent help on Linux-LAN
In-Reply-To: <BAY132-W328AF76C516031987572ADCC770@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY132-W1608AD63F2BB4362777B46CC770@phx.gbl>
	<446cb7260711280726l60288009p54f6af63e1a75f87@mail.gmail.com>
	<BAY132-W328AF76C516031987572ADCC770@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <200711291344.17455.knura@yahoo.com>

An ascii art of your network topology would have given a much clearer  
picture and help us understand your problem.  BTW, I am curious as to 
why you have complicated your network so much?  Is this a lab 
assignment question?

On Wednesday 28 Nov 2007, swapan karmakar wrote:
> two LANS-192.168.1.0 series and 172.16.1.0 series
                                  ^^^^^^^^^^
This is a class B network 172.16.0.0 unless you are subnetting it.

> one proxy server whose ip is 172.16.10.1 is connected to braodband
> internet (modem).. 

So does your proxy have 2 NICs?  one bridged to the DSL modem and acting 
as WAN interface and the other one connected to your own "router" 
system?

> one system acting as router has eth0=172.16.1.1 & 
> eth1=192.168.1.1 172.16.1.1 system is getting net via 172.16.10.1
> the 192.168.1.2 client is not able to access the internet...is it
> possible to acess internet via 192.168.1.1...? 

The proxy server needs to know that 192.168.1.0 network is behind 
172.16.1.1 (man route on how to do this).  Otherwise how will the proxy 
know where to send the packets for 192.168.1.0?  Alternately, do NAT on 
your "router" system on iface 172.16.1.1 - all traffic from 192.168.1. 
will appear as coming from 172.16.1.1

> in present case , i 
> want to redirect 192.168.1.2 to 172.16.1.1:3128 to access net..

Do not understand what you are trying to do here.  Suggest, first solve 
your basic routing table entries and then tackle above.

> ISP has given two dns address & one router address.

This would be on the proxy server.  Your def gw on the 192.168.1. 
network s/b 192.168.1.1 and on the 172.16. network s/b 172.16.10.1

Let us know when you solve the problem (along with your solution) to 
help others who may run into a similar issue.

HTH,
Arun Khan

one proxy server whose ip is 172.16.10.1 is connected to braodband internet
(modem)..
one system acting as router has eth0=172.16.1.1 & eth1=192.168.1.1
172.16.1.1 system is getting net via 172.16.10.1
the 192.168.1.2 client is not able to access the internet...is it possible
to acess internet via 192.168.1.1...?
in present case , i want to redirect 192.168.1.2 to 172.16.1.1:3128 to
access net..


Well i think i understand  it now .did you enable ip forwarding in the
system having the two Ethernet cards?

And make sure that the gateway is defined. check the  out put of the route
command to make this sure.

Regards
Raj

From mailing.vivek at gmail.com  Thu Nov 29 16:56:20 2007
From: mailing.vivek at gmail.com (vivek khurana)
Date: Thu Nov 29 16:56:38 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [fossconf] Go with the World
In-Reply-To: <474BC07F.6010703@gmail.com>
References: <474BC07F.6010703@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3e4fd9970711290326r4b0e553fy4098375f58ee0f69@mail.gmail.com>

>
> I do understand that things have gone a little far. Renaming the
> conference may be very difficult at this stage. We can consider it as an
> option for next year, or conduct another conference or something similar.


 Why wait till next year ? You can create a sub/mini conference this
year under fossconf. You need to do the following

0) Gather momentum for the idea.
1) Identify the agenda for the sub-conf
2) Identify the infrastructure required and approach the organizers
for arranging the infrastructure.
3) Identify the speakers and decide whether you want it to be a invite
only speakers or any one can become a speaker.
4) Create a procedure for verifying the credentials for the chosen speakers

You have 2 months to market the subconf if you act now. So, lets not
wait a whole year...

regards
VK

On Nov 28, 2007 8:55 AM, Bama <chorse@gmail.com> wrote:
> I've installed ubuntu 6.06 and had dlink wireless router connected to a bsnl
> modem, and was quite happy with browsing until I installed azerus. I'm not
> sure about the ports or the firewall it triggered, apparently now I'm not

 Azureus will not automatically change firewall settings. Are you sure
you did not change anything ? Also, try turning off UnPnP from the
router.

 As a first measure just check your

1) Routing settings
2) Nameservers
3) Proxy settings. (carefully check if you made any environmental wide
proxy settings).

Also, please upgrade the box, azureus version in ubuntu 6.06 is old and buggy.

> able to use browsers, but from commmand line I could ping almost all sites.

 Can you open website from command line browsers like lynx and elinks
? If not then you need to contact the ISP.
